Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat: Obligation on Nisab After a Year
Defining Zakat, its obligation, nisab, and hawl condition with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for zakat obligation (nisab and hawl) and explain why the term 'wajib' in this context means fard.

Core Idea
Zakat is fard on every nisab that completes a lunar year – no nisab, no year, no zakat.

This lesson opens the Book of Zakat in the classical text. The commentator explains why zakat follows prayer, defines key terms, and establishes that zakat is a definitive obligation (fard) on those who own a minimum amount of wealth (nisab) for one full lunar year (hawl). Two essential conditions must be met before zakat becomes due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn states: 'Zakat is not obligatory except on a nisab that has passed a year.' This is the core ruling. Recognize that the ruling is conditional upon two factors: nisab and hawl.
The ruling is stated in the negative (la tajibu) to emphasize that absence of either condition lifts the obligation.
2
Clarify 'Wajib' vs. 'Fard'
The commentator explains that 'wajib' here means fard (definitive obligation from qat'i evidence), not the technical Hanafi 'wajib' which is based on zanni evidence. This is because zakat is a pillar of Islam, proven by mutawatir texts.
In Hanafi usul, 'fard' and 'wajib' are distinct categories; failure to distinguish here leads to a major conceptual error.
3
Define Nisab
Nisab is the minimum amount of wealth (e.g., 200 dirhams of silver, 20 dinars of gold) below which zakat is not due. The commentator notes that specific nisab values for different types of wealth will be given later.
Nisab thresholds are specified by the Prophet (peace be upon him) and are not subject to analogy.
4
Define Hawl (the Yearly Cycle)
Hawl means that a full lunar year must pass over the nisab for zakat to become due. The condition is proven by the hadith of Ali (ra) and the practice of Abu Bakr (ra).
Hawl is a condition (shart) for obligation, not a pillar of the zakat payment itself.
5
Review the Proofs
The commentator cites Quranic verses (2:43, 9:103) for the obligation of zakat itself, and hadith for the hawl condition. He notes that the hadith on zakat are numerous, reaching tawatur.
The strength of proof (qat'i thubut and qat'i dalala) confirms that zakat is fard, not wajib in the technical sense.

Source Text

(٢) قوله : هي لا تجب إلا ... الخ ؛ المراد بالوجوب هاهنا الافتراض، لا الوجوب الاصطلاحي الثابت لزومهُ بالدلائل الظنية، فإنه لا خلاف في كون الزَّكاة فرضاً لقوله وَمَاتُوا الزَّكَوةَ ) ، وقوله : خُذْ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةً تُطَهَرُهُمْ وَتُزَكِّيهِم بِهَا ) ، والأخبار في هذا الباب كثيرة بلغت إلى حد التواتر المعنوي.

Book of Zakat: It is not obligatory except on a nisab that has passed a year. Book of Zakat: (It is not obligatory except) on a nisab that has passed a year. [1] His saying: Book of Zakat; when he finished mentioning one of the pillars of Islam, which is prayer, he began the second of them, which is zakat, and he paired it with it because of their pairing in His saying: {Establish prayer and pay zakat}, and he gave precedence to prayer because it is the most virtuous and most important of the pillars. Zakat originally means growth, and since zakat is a cause for the growth of reward in the Hereafter and the growth of wealth in this world by compensation, it was named thus. [2] His saying: It is not obligatory except... etc.; what is meant by obligation here is farḍ (definitive obligation), not the technical wujūb established by probable evidences, because there is no disagreement that zakat is farḍ due to His saying: {Pay zakat} and His saying: {Take from their wealth a charity to purify them and cleanse them thereby}, and the reports on this topic are numerous, reaching the level of moral tawātur. [3] His saying: nisāb; with a kasra on the nūn: a term for the amount below which zakat is not obligatory. Reports have come that zakat is due on gold, silver, grazing livestock, and others in specific amounts, not obligatory below that, as you will come across in its proper place, God willing. [4] His saying: ḥawlī; with a shadda on the yā: it is relative to al-ḥawl (with a fatḥa), meaning the year, i.e., a nisab upon which a year has passed. So zakat is not obligatory on a nisab that has not had a year pass over it; due to the hadith: (1) Al-Baqara: from verse 43. (2) Al-Tawba: from verse 103. (3) From Ali (may God be pleased with him) who said: 'If you have two hundred dirhams and a year passes over them, then five dirhams are due, and nothing is due on you, meaning in gold, until you have twenty dinars. If you have twenty dinars and a year passes over them, then half a dinar is due.' In Sunan Abi Dawud (2:100) and al-Ahadith al-Mukhtara (2:154). And from al-Qasim: That Abu Bakr al-Siddiq would not take zakat from wealth until a year had passed over it.' In Muwatta Malik (1:245).
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya on the matn of al-Wiqaya, opening the Book of Zakat. The commentator begins by explaining why zakat follows prayer in the text: because both are paired in the Quran (Surah al-Baqara 2:43) and prayer is the more excellent pillar. He then gives the linguistic meaning of zakat as 'growth' and notes that it is named so because it causes growth in reward and wealth. The core ruling: Zakat is obligatory only on a nisab that has completed a full lunar year (hawl). The commentator clarifies that the term 'wujub' here means fard (definitive obligation from qat'i evidence), not the technical Hanafi 'wajib' which is from zanni evidence. This is important because in Hanafi fiqh, 'wajib' is a distinct category below fard, but zakat is fard according to all, due to clear Quranic commands and numerous hadith reaching tawatur. The nisab is defined as the minimum amount of wealth (gold, silver, livestock, etc.) below which no zakat is due; specific nisab values will be given later in the text. The condition of hawl (yearly passage) is proven by the hadith of Ali (ra) specifying the zakat on 200 dirhams after a year, and the practice of Abu Bakr (ra) not taking zakat until a year had passed. Thus, the two fundamental conditions for zakat obligation are: (1) possession of a nisab, and (2) the passage of a full lunar year over that nisab.

Key Terms
الزكاة (al-zakat): A fixed portion of wealth prescribed by Allah to be given to specific categories, linguistically meaning growth and purification.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth (e.g., 200 dirhams of silver, 20 dinars of gold) below which zakat is not obligatory.
حولي (hawli): Relating to a lunar year; the condition that a full year must pass over the nisab for zakat to become due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the commentator clarify about the word 'wujub' in the phrase 'la tajibu illa fi nisab hawli'?
A) It means the technical Hanafi 'wajib' (obligatory but from zanni evidence).
B) It means 'fard' (definitive obligation) because zakat is a pillar of Islam.
C) It means 'sunnah mu'akkadah' (emphasized sunnah).
D) It means 'mubah' (permissible).

Key Takeaway
Zakat is fard only when two conditions are met: owning a nisab and the passage of a full lunar year.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Conditions for Zakat Obligation: Nisab, Hawl, and More
Defines the essential conditions for zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for zakat to be obligatory according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Zakat is fard only on productive wealth that exceeds basic needs, with a minimum threshold (nisab) held for a year.

Zakat is the second pillar of Islam, paired with prayer in the Qur'an. Its obligation depends on specific conditions that ensure it is levied only on wealth that can sustain payment without hardship. This lesson unpacks those conditions from the classical Hanafi text, clarifying the precise meaning of obligation (fard, not technical wajib) and the evidence from hadith and practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
The passage clarifies that 'obligation' here means fard (definitive), not technical wajib. Zakat is fard ‘ayn on every eligible Muslim, proven by Qur'an and mutawatir hadith.
Distinguish fard from wajib: fard is proven by definitive evidence (Qat'i), wajib by probabilistic (Zanni).
2
Define nisab and its textual basis
Nisab is the minimum amount of wealth below which zakat is not due. The passage mentions that specific nisab amounts for gold, silver, and livestock are established by hadith.
Nisab varies by wealth type; e.g., 200 dirhams for silver, 20 dinars for gold.
3
Analyze the hawl condition and its proof
Hawl means a full lunar year must pass over the nisab. The hadith from ‘Ali (ra) and the practice of Abu Bakr (ra) are cited as evidence.
The conditional phrasing in the hadith (if... and a year passes) indicates the passing of a year is a condition for obligation.
4
Explore the additional conditions: excess over basic needs and productivity
Wealth must be surplus to basic needs (hāja aṣliyya) and must be productive (nāmin), actually or potentially. If wealth is needed for essentials or is idle, zakat is not due.
Basic needs include food, shelter, clothing, debt repayment; productivity includes trade goods, livestock, or capital that can grow.
5
Synthesize the conditions into a coherent framework
All four conditions (nisab, hawl, excess over needs, productivity) must be met for zakat to be obligatory. They are derived from hadith, ijma, and the principle of avoiding hardship.
These conditions are agreed upon by the Hanafi school and generally accepted by other schools, though details may differ.

The Book of Zakat
It is not obligatory except in [a] nisab [that is] hawlī.
(It is not obligatory except) in [a] nisab [that is] hawlī.
[4]
[1] His saying: The Book of Zakat; when he finished mentioning one of the pillars of Islam, which is prayer, he began the second of them, which is zakat, and he paired it with it due to their pairing in His statement: 'And establish prayer and give zakat', and he gave precedence to prayer because it is the most virtuous and important of the pillars. And zakat originally means growth, and since zakat is a cause for the growth of reward in the Hereafter and the growth of wealth in this world through compensation, it was named with it.
(2) His saying: It is not obligatory except... etc.; what is meant by obligation here is fard (definitive obligation), not the technical wajib (established by probabilistic proofs), for there is no disagreement that zakat is fard due to His statement 'and give zakat' and His statement 'Take from their wealth a charity to purify them and sanctify them with it', and the reports on this topic are numerous, reaching the level of tawatur bi al-ma‘na.
[3] His saying: nisab; with kasra of the nun: a term for a quantity below which zakat is not obligatory, and reports have come that for gold, silver, grazing animals, and others, there is a specific amount for which zakat is obligatory, and it is not obligatory below it, as you will come across in its proper place, God willing.
[4] His saying: hawlī; with tashdid on the ya: relating to al-hawl (year), meaning a nisab upon which a year has passed, so it is not obligatory on a nisab upon which a year has not passed (3); due to the hadith: (From ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'If you have two hundred dirhams and a year passes over them, then five dirhams are due on them, and nothing is due on you, meaning for gold until you have twenty dinars, and if you have twenty dinars and a year passes over them, then half a dinar is due on them' in Sunan Abi Dawud (2:100) and al-Ahadith al-Mukhtara (2:154). And from al-Qasim: 'Abu Bakr al-Siddiq would not take zakat from wealth until a year had passed over it' in Muwatta Malik (1:245).
[PAGE_394]
394
‘Umda al-Ri‘āya ‘alā Sharḥ al-Wiqāya
excess over his basic need.
excess over his basic need (1).
Know that zakat is not obligatory except in [a] nisab [that is] productive, and [with] the passing of a year.
(1) 'Zakat is not due on wealth until a year passes over it', reported by Abu Dawud, Ahmad, al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi, Ibn Majah, and others with similar wording.
[1] His saying: basic need; it is what repells destruction from a person actually, like maintenance, houses of residence, weapons, and clothes needed to repel heat or cold, or potentially like debt, for the debtor needs to repay it with the nisab in his hand to repel from himself imprisonment, which is like destruction.
If he has dirhams that are due to be spent on those needs, they become like non-existent, just as water that is due to be spent on thirst becomes like non-existent and it is permissible for him to perform tayammum in that case, as in Sharh Majma‘ al-Bahrayn by Ibn Malik, and this condition for the obligation of zakat is unanimously agreed upon.
[2] His saying: productive, meaning described by growth actually or potentially, for if zakat were obligatory on non-productive wealth, it would consume the wealth and annihilate it, which is a great hardship, and it is removed from us by the text of the Qur’an. [3] His saying: and the passing of a year; the year is called hawlan because the states change in it, just as it is called sanah (with two fathas) due to the occurrence of the “sunna” (change) of things in it, and it is also called ‘ām because the sun “‘āma” (traversed) the entire zodiac, as al-‘Aynī mentioned in al-Bināya Sharḥ al-Hidāya (3:11).
And from Ibn ‘Umar, he used to say: 'Zakat is not due on wealth until a year passes over it' in al-Muwatta (1:246).
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling exposition from the beginning of the Book of Zakat in ‘Umda al-Ri‘āya. The author first explains why zakat follows prayer in the text: because the Qur’an pairs them, and prayer is more virtuous. Then he clarifies that the word 'obligation' here means fard (definitive obligation), not the technical wajib, as zakat is established by definitive proofs (Qur’an and mutawatir hadith). The term 'zakat' originally means growth, and it is named so because it increases reward and wealth.
The first condition for zakat is nisab (minimum threshold). The text defines nisab as an amount below which no zakat is due, and it varies for gold, silver, livestock, etc. The second condition is hawl (passing of a full lunar year). The hadith from ‘Ali and the practice of Abu Bakr are cited to prove that a year must pass. The commentary on page 394 adds further conditions: excess over basic needs (hājat aṣliyya) and productivity (nāmi). Basic needs include actual necessities like food, housing, clothing, and potential needs like debt repayment. If wealth is needed for these, it is considered non-existent and no zakat is due. Productivity (growth) can be actual (like trade profits) or potential (like livestock offspring). If zakat were on non-productive wealth, it would cause hardship, which is removed by the Qur’an (the verse 'God does not burden a soul beyond its capacity'). The condition of hawl is also emphasized with additional hadith. All these conditions are essential for zakat to be obligatory.

Key Terms
زكاة (zakāt): Linguistically: growth. Legally: a specific obligatory payment on specified wealth to specified recipients.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth (e.g., 200 dirhams silver, 20 dinars gold) that triggers zakat obligation.
حولي (ḥawlī): Relating to a full lunar year; the condition that the nisab must be in one's possession for a complete year.
حاجة أصلية (ḥāja aṣliyya): Basic need that is essential for survival or preservation of dignity, such as food, shelter, clothing, and tools of trade. Wealth needed for these is excluded from zakat.
نام (nāmin): Productive/growing wealth, either actually (e.g., trade goods, livestock) or potentially (e.g., gold/silver for trade).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'hāja aṣliyya' (basic need) that excludes wealth from zakat?
A) Luxury items and savings
B) Items that repel destruction actually or potentially, such as food, housing, debt repayment
C) Only food and drink
D) Wealth that is not productive

Key Takeaway
Zakat is fard on wealth that meets four conditions: nisab, hawl, excess over basic needs, and productivity; each condition has textual evidence and prevents undue hardship.

Conditions for Zakat: Surplus, Growth, and the Year
Commentary on three conditions for zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for zakat obligation in the Hanafi school and explain why the year alone is insufficient without the additional conditions of thamaniyya, sa'ima, or niyat tijara.

Core Idea
Zakat requires surplus, growth, and a year — but the year is a proxy, not sufficient alone.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' unpacks the three fundamental conditions for zakat as explained in al-Hidayah. You will explore the definitions of basic need, growth, and the lunar year, and understand a critical observation that the year is necessary but not sufficient — additional qualitative conditions must also be met.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Locate the three conditions stated in the opening: surplus (fadlan 'an hajah), growth (nam), and year (hawl).
These are the main conditions mentioned in the matn.
2
Define 'basic need' (al-hajat al-asliyyah)
Understand that it includes both actual and potential necessities, and see the analogy with water for tayammum.
This condition is unanimously agreed upon.
3
Understand 'growth' (nama')
Recognize that it includes actual and potential growth; the Quranic principle of no hardship prevents taxing non-growing wealth.
Growth can be actual (profit) or potential (breeding livestock).
4
Analyze the year condition
See the hadith from Ibn Umar and the explanation that the year is a proxy for growth due to seasonal price changes.
The hadith is from al-Muwatta, transmitted as ahad.
5
Evaluate the critique
Note that the author ('fihi nazar') clarifies that the year alone is insufficient; additional conditions (thamaniyya, sa'ima, niyat tijara) are required.
This critique refines the apparent meaning of al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أنَّ الزَّكَاةَ لا تَجِبُ إلا في نصاب نام، والحول فاضلاً عن حاجتِهِ الأصلية. [١]قوله : حاجته الأصلية ؛ هي ما يدفع الهلاك عن الإنسان تحقيقاً كالنفقة، ودور السكني، وآلات الحرب، والنياب المحتاج إليها لدفع الحر أو البرد ، أو تقديراً کالدين، فإنَّ المديون محتاج إلى قضاء ما في يده من النصاب دفعاً عن نفسه الحبس الذي هو كالهلاك. فإذا كان له دراهم مستحقه يصرفها إلى تلك الحوائج صارت كالمعدومة، كما أنَّ الماء المستحق يصرفه إلى العطش كان كالمعدوم وجاز عنده التيمم، كذا في «شرح مجمع البحرين» لابن ملك، وهذا الشرط لوجوب الزكاة مجمع عليه. [٢]قوله: نام، أي موصوف بالنَّماء تحقيقاً كان أو تقديراً، فإنه لو وجبت الزَّكاةُ في غير نام لأكلت المال وأفنته، وهو حرج عظيم، وهو مرفوع عنا بنص القرآن. [٣] قوله : والحول ؛ إنّما سُمِّيَّت السَّنةُ حولاً ؛ لأنَّ الأحوال تحوَّلُ فيها، كما أن تسميتها بالسَّنة بفتحتين لوجودِ سنة الأشياء فيها، وهو التَّغير، وتُسمَّى عاماً أيضاً ؛ لأنَّ الشَّمس عامت فقطعت جميع الفلك، كذا ذكرَهُ العَيْنِيُّ في «البنايةِ شرح الهداية). وعن ابن عمر كان يقول : «لا تجب في مال زكاة حتى يحول عليه الحول» في «الموطأ». [۱] هو الممكن من الاستنماء؛ لاشتماله على الفصول الأربعة، والغالب فيها تفاوت الأسعار، فاقيم مقامَ النَّماء ، فأدير الحكم عليه، هذا هو المذكور في «الهداية). وفيه نظر؛ لأنَّ هذا يقتضي أنه إذا حالَ الحولُ على النصابِ تَجِبُ الزَّكاة سواء وُجِدَ النَّماء ، أو لم يوجد [1]قوله : هو الممكن ؛ اسم فاعل من التمكين، أي هو الذي تحصل به القدرة على استنماء المال أي طلب نمائه. [٢] قوله : لاشتماله ؛ أي لاشتمال الحول على الفصول الأربعة المختلفة، الربيع والصيف والشتاء والخريف، فإنَّ النّجاراتِ ربّما يتهيأ الاسترباح فيها في الصيف دون العكس، وكذلك في الربيع والخريف، فلذلك عَلّقَ الاستنماء بحول، ثمَّ لَمَّا أقيم حولان الحول مقامَ الاستنماء فبعد ذلك لم تعتبر حقيقة الاستنماء، حتى إذا ظهر النَّماءُ أو لم يظهر تجب فيه الزكاة. كذا في «البناية». [٣] قوله : فأقيم ؛ أي جعل الحول قائماً مقام النماء؛ لكونه سببه لحصوله فيه غالباً، وإن لم يحصل أحياناً، فإذا حال الحول وجبت الزَّكاة. (٤) قوله : وفيه نظر؛ حاصلُ الإيرادِ أن عبارة «الهداية» تدل على أن الحول أقيمَ مقامَ النَّماء ، وإِنَّ الزَّكَاةَ تجب عند مضي الحول، مع أنه ليس كذلك، فإنّه لا يكفي لوجوبها حولان الحول على النّصاب بل له شروط أخرى لا تجب بدونها. وباقتراح آخر يدل قوله: «فأدير الحكم عليه» بحسب ظاهره أن وجوب الزكاة دائر مع الحول وجوداً وعدماً، مع أنَّ الدَّوران عدماً وإن كان صحيحاً فإنّه إذا لم يوجد حولانه لم تجب الزكاة، لكن الدوران وجوداً لا يصح، فليس أن كل ما حال عليه الحول وجبت فيه الزكاة، فإنّه لا بدَّ مع الحول من شيء آخر وهو الثَّمنيَّةُ أو السوم، أو نية التجارة.
Know that zakat is not obligatory except on a growing nisab, and the year, surplus to one's basic need. [1] His statement: 'his basic need' – it is what wards off destruction from a person realistically, like maintenance, residential houses, weapons of war, and garments needed to ward off heat or cold, or by estimation like debt, for the debtor needs to repay it from the nisab in his possession to ward off imprisonment which is like destruction. So if he has dirhams that are rightful to be spent on those needs, they become like non-existent, just as water that is rightful to be spent on thirst becomes like non-existent and it is permissible for him to perform tayammum. This is stated in 'Sharh Majma' al-Bahrayn' by Ibn Malik, and this condition for the obligation of zakat is agreed upon. [2] His statement: 'growing' – that is, described with growth actually or virtually, because if zakat were obligatory on non-growing wealth, it would consume and annihilate wealth, which is a great hardship, and it is removed from us by the text of the Quran. [3] His statement: 'and the year' – the year is called 'hawl' because states change in it, just as it is called 'sanah' with two fatha due to the occurrence of the 'sanah' (change) of things, which is change, and it is also called 'am' because the sun travels and cuts across the entire firmament. Thus al-Ayni mentioned in 'al-Binayah Sharh al-Hidayah'. And from Ibn Umar he used to say: 'Zakat is not obligatory on wealth until a year passes over it' in al-Muwatta. [1] It is that which can possibly produce growth, because it includes the four seasons, and in them prices mostly fluctuate, so it was made to stand in the place of growth, and the ruling was made to revolve upon it. This is what is mentioned in al-Hidayah. And there is a consideration in it, because this implies that when a year passes over the nisab, zakat becomes obligatory whether growth occurred or not. [1] His statement: 'it is that which can possibly' – an active participle from tamkeen, meaning it is that by which one gains the ability to seek growth of wealth, i.e., to seek its increase. [2] His statement: 'because it includes' – meaning because the year includes the four different seasons, spring, summer, winter, and autumn, for trades perhaps profit can be obtained in summer but not vice versa, and similarly in spring and autumn, therefore seeking growth was attached to a year. Then, when the passing of the year was made to stand in the place of actual growth, after that the reality of growth was not considered, so whether growth appears or not, zakat is obligatory on it. This is stated in al-Binayah. [3] His statement: 'so it was made to stand' – meaning the year was made to stand in the place of growth because it is usually the cause for its occurrence, even if it sometimes does not occur, so when the year passes, zakat becomes obligatory. (4) His statement: 'and there is a consideration' – the essence of the objection is that the phrase of al-Hidayah indicates that the year was made to stand in place of growth and that zakat becomes obligatory at the passing of the year, while it is not so, for it is not sufficient for its obligation that the year passes over the nisab, but there are other conditions without which it does not become obligatory. And by another formulation, his statement: 'so the ruling was made to revolve upon it' apparently means that the obligation of zakat revolves with the year in existence and non-existence, while the revolving in non-existence is correct, because if its passing does not occur, zakat is not obligatory, but the revolving in existence is not correct, for not every wealth over which a year passes has zakat obligatory on it, because along with the year there must be something else: being a thamani (monetary) or grazing livestock, or intention of trade.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' explains the three fundamental conditions for the obligation of zakat as derived from the matn of al-Hidayah. The commentary begins by defining 'basic need' (hajat asliyya): it includes all essentials that preserve life, both actual (like food, housing, clothing) and potential (like debt, which if unpaid leads to imprisonment). If wealth is required to meet these needs, it is considered non-existent for zakat purposes, analogous to water reserved for thirst which permits tayammum. This condition is unanimously agreed upon. Next, the passage defines 'growing' (nam): wealth must be capable of increase, either actually (like trade goods) or virtually (like livestock or gold). Obligating zakat on non-growing wealth would consume capital, which contradicts Quranic mercy. Finally, the 'year' (hawl): the lunar year is named 'hawl' because of the changes it brings. A hadith from Ibn Umar establishes that zakat is not due until a year passes. The commentary then explains that the year serves as a proxy for growth since seasonal price fluctuations typically allow profit. However, the author raises a critical observation ('fihi nazar') on the phrasing of al-Hidayah, which might suggest that the mere passage of a year is sufficient. The correct position is that additional conditions are required: the wealth must be thamaniyya (monetary, e.g., gold, silver, or currency), or sa'ima (grazing livestock), or trade goods with intention of trade. Thus, the year is necessary but not sufficient.

Key Terms
الحاجة الأصلية (al-hajat al-asliyyah): Basic needs: what wards off destruction, actual (food, housing, clothing) or potential (debt).
النماء (al-nama'): Growth: actual increase (like profit) or potential for increase (like livestock breeding).
الحول (al-hawl): The lunar year; its passage is a proxy for growth due to seasonal price changes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author mean by 'hawl' in the context of zakat?
A) The lunar year
B) The season of spring
C) The day of Eid
D) The month of Ramadan

Key Takeaway
Zakat obligation requires three conditions: surplus to basic needs, capacity for growth, and passage of one year, but the year alone is insufficient without additional qualitative conditions (thamaniyya, sa'ima, or niyat tijara).

Zakat — Almsgiving

Hawl as Proxy for Growth: Conditions for Zakat
Defends Al-Hidayah's statement on hawl as proxy for growth in zakat conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three additional conditions required alongside the hawl for zakat obligation and explain why the hawl is considered a proxy for growth.

Core Idea
The hawl replaces actual growth, but three conditions—thamaniyyah, sawm, or trade intention—are essential for zakat.

This passage defends Al-Hidayah's statement that the passage of a lunar year (hawl) serves as a substitute for actual growth in wealth for zakat. An objector mistakenly thought Al-Hidayah meant the hawl alone suffices. The author clarifies that Al-Hidayah only intended to explain why the hawl is chosen, and that the three specific conditions—gold/silver by nature, grazing livestock, or trade intention—are necessary. Understanding this distinction protects against oversimplifying the conditions of zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim from Al-Hidayah
Al-Hidayah says the hawl is made a substitute for actual growth because the year includes seasons of price fluctuation. Determine what this claim implies about the relationship between hawl and growth.
The claim is about why hawl is used, not about all conditions.
2
State the objection raised
The objector (commentator) argues that Al-Hidayah's wording suggests the hawl alone triggers zakat, which is false. Articulate the objection clearly.
The objection hinges on interpreting 'the ruling revolves upon the year' as exclusive.
3
Analyze the defense of Al-Hidayah
The defender explains that Al-Hidayah's purpose was only to justify using hawl as a proxy, not to list all conditions. The text elsewhere mentions the additional conditions. Paraphrase this response.
The defense uses the analogy of travel licenses where travel itself substitutes for hardship.
4
Identify the three additional conditions
From the commentary, extract the three conditions: thamaniyyah (gold/silver by nature), sawm (grazing livestock), and niyyat al-tijarah (trade intention). Understand what each entails.
‘Thamaniyyah’ excludes coins (fulus) because they are prices by custom, not by nature.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Use the conditions to determine whether zakat is due on a given asset. For example, silver coins held for a year: thamaniyyah applies, so zakat is due.
Gold and silver are always zakatable if they reach nisab and one year passes.

كتاب الزكاة شروط الزكاة هو الممكن من الاستنماء؛ لاشتماله على الفصول الأربعة، والغالب فيها تفاوت الأسعار، فأقيم مقام النماء، فأدير الحكم عليه، هذا هو المذكور في «الهداية». وفيه نظر؛ لأن هذا يقتضي أنه إذا حال الحول على النصاب تجب الزكاة سواء وجد النماء أو لم يوجد. [1] قوله: هو الممكن؛ اسم فاعل من التمكين، أي هو الذي تحصل به القدرة على استنماء المال أي طلب نمائه. [2] قوله: لاشتماله؛ أي لاشتمال الحول على الفصول الأربعة المختلفة، الربيع والصيف والشتاء والخريف، فإن التجارات ربما يتهيأ الاسترباح فيها في الصيف دون العكس، وكذلك في الربيع والخريف، فلذلك علق الاستنماء بحول، ثم لما أقيم حولان الحول مقام الاستنماء فبعد ذلك لم تعتبر حقيقة الاستنماء، حتى إذا ظهر النماء أو لم يظهر تجب فيه الزكاة. كذا في «البناية». [3] قوله: فأقيم؛ أي جعل الحول قائماً مقام النماء؛ لكونه سببه لحصوله فيه غالباً، وإن لم يحصل أحياناً، فإذا حال الحول وجبت الزكاة. [4] قوله: وفيه نظر؛ حاصل الإيراد أن عبارة «الهداية» تدل على أن الحول أقيم مقام النماء، وإن الزكاة تجب عند مضي الحول، مع أنه ليس كذلك، فإنه لا يكفي لوجوبها حولان الحول على النصاب بل له شروط أخرى لا تجب بدونها. وبعبارة أخرى يدل قوله: «فأدير الحكم عليه» بحسب ظاهره أن وجوب الزكاة دائر مع الحول وجوداً وعدماً، مع أن الدوران عدماً وإن كان صحيحاً فإنه إذا لم يوجد حولانه لم تجب الزكاة، لكن الدوران وجوداً لا يصح، فليس أن كل ما حال عليه الحول وجبت فيه الزكاة، فإنه لا بد مع الحول من شيء آخر وهو الثمنية أو السوم، أو نية التجارة. كما في السفر، فإنه أقيم مقام المشقة، فيدار الرخصة عليه سواء وجد المشقة أم لا، لكن ليس كذلك، بل لا بد مع الحول من شيء آخر، وهو الثمنية كما في الثمنين: أي الذهب والفضة، أو السوم كما في الأنعام، أو نية التجارة في غير ما ذكرنا. ولا يخفى على المتدرب أن هذا الإيراد مدفوع بأدنى توجه، فإن غرض صاحب «الهداية» من العبارة المذكورة ليس إلا ذكر أن الحول قائم مقام النماء، والنماء الحقيقي غير معتبر، وأن الحكم دائر على الحول لا على النماء، وهو حاصل منه. وأما كونه مشروطاً بأمر آخر أو غير مشروط فهو بمعزل عنه، وقد دل كلام «الهداية» قبل هذه العبارة وبعدها على اشتراط الشروط الأخرى التي ذكرها الشارح له كما لا يخفى على من طالعها. فإن قلت: غرض الشارح أن هذه العبارة قاصرة غير وافية. قلت: لا بل هي وافية بما قصد منها، ولا بأس بعدم دلالتها على ما لم يقصد منها، لا سيما إذا دل عليه كلام سابق أو لاحق. [1] قوله: كما في السفر؛ تنظير لما نحن فيه، وتأييد له، فإن الرخص المختصة بالسفر شرعت تيسيراً لحصول المشقة في السفر، ثم اعتبر لها نفس السفر إقامة للسبب مقام المسبب، فكلما وجد السفر ثبت حكم الرخص للمسافر، وإن لم توجد المشقة حقيقة. [2] قوله: لكن ليس كذلك؛ أي ليس مجرد حولان الحول كافياً لوجوب الزكاة. [3] قوله: وهو الثمنية...الخ؛ حاصله: أن الزكاة لا تجب في مال وإن بلغ مقدار النصاب، وحال عليه الحول أيضاً إلا إذا وجد ثلاثة أشياء: أحدها: الثمنية؛ وهو أن يكون المال ثمناً خلقة بأن يكون مخلوقاً لأن يجعل ثمناً وعوضاً في العقود والتجارات، وتشترى بها الأشياء، وهو الذهب والفضة، فتلزم فيهما الزكاة كيفما أمسكهما، ولو للنفقة إذا حال عليهما الحول، وبلغ نصاباً واحترز بقوله: «خلقة» عن الفلوس، فإنها أثمان عرفاً واصطلاحاً، لا خلقة.
The book of Zakat: Conditions of Zakat. It is that which enables seeking growth; because the year includes the four seasons, and prices often fluctuate within them, so the year is made a substitute for growth, and the ruling is made to revolve upon it. This is what is mentioned in Al-Hidayah. And there is a critique: because this implies that if the year passes on the nisab, zakat becomes obligatory whether growth occurs or not. [1] He said: 'it is that which enables' – a verbal noun from tamkin, meaning that by which one gains the ability to seek growth of wealth, i.e., to seek its increase. [2] He said: 'because it includes' – i.e., because the year includes the four different seasons, spring, summer, winter, and autumn, for businesses may become profitable in summer but not the opposite, and similarly in spring and autumn. Therefore, seeking growth was attached to the year. Then when the passing of the year was made a substitute for seeking growth, the reality of growth was no longer considered, so whether growth appears or not, zakat becomes obligatory. Thus in Al-Binayah. [3] He said: 'so it was made' – i.e., the year was made a substitute for growth because it is usually the cause of its occurrence, even if it does not occur sometimes. So when the year passes, zakat becomes obligatory. [4] He said: 'and there is a critique' – the summary of the objection is that the expression of Al-Hidayah indicates that the year is made a substitute for growth, and zakat is obligatory upon the passage of the year, but it is not so, because the passage of the year on the nisab is not sufficient for its obligation; rather, it has other conditions without which it is not obligatory. In other words, his statement 'so the ruling is made to revolve upon it' apparently indicates that the obligation of zakat revolves with the year in existence and non-existence, whereas the revolving in non-existence, though correct—if the year does not pass, zakat is not obligatory—but the revolving in existence is not correct, for not everything upon which the year passes has zakat obligatory; rather, along with the year, something else is necessary, which is thamaniyyah (being a price), or sawm (grazing), or intention of trade. Just as in travel: it is made a substitute for hardship, so the license revolves upon it whether hardship is found or not. But it is not so; rather, along with the year, something else is necessary: thamaniyyah as in the two prices (gold and silver), or sawm as in cattle, or intention of trade in what we have not mentioned. And it is not hidden from the trainee that this objection is repelled with the slightest attention, for the purpose of the author of Al-Hidayah from the mentioned expression is only to state that the year is a substitute for growth, and real growth is not considered, and that the ruling revolves upon the year, not upon growth. This is what he intended. As for it being conditioned by another matter or not, it is apart from that. And the speech of Al-Hidayah before and after this expression has indicated the other conditions that the commentator mentioned, as is not hidden from one who peruses it. If you say: the commentator's purpose is that this expression is deficient and insufficient. I say: rather, it is sufficient for what is intended from it, and there is no harm in it not indicating what was not intended, especially if previous or subsequent speech indicates it. [1] He said: 'as in travel' – an analogy for our subject and support for it, for the licenses specific to travel were legislated to facilitate the occurrence of hardship in travel, then travel itself was considered an establishment of the cause in place of the effect. So whenever travel exists, the ruling of licenses is confirmed for the traveler, even if hardship is not actually found. [2] He said: 'but it is not so' – meaning that mere passage of the year is not sufficient for zakat obligation. [3] He said: 'and it is thamaniyyah...etc.' – its summary: that zakat is not obligatory on wealth even if it reaches the amount of nisab and the year has passed upon it, unless three conditions exist: first, thamaniyyah: that the wealth is a price by nature, i.e., created to be a price and compensation in contracts and trades, and things are bought with it, and it is gold and silver. Zakat is obligatory on them however they are held, even for spending, if the year passes on them and they reach nisab. And by his saying 'by nature' he excludes coins (fulus), for they are prices customarily and conventionally, not by nature.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a statement from Al-Hidayah regarding the role of the hawl (year) in zakat. It begins by stating that the hawl is considered a proxy (qaim maqam) for actual growth (nama), because the year typically encompasses seasons of profit fluctuation. Then an objection is raised: the wording of Al-Hidayah seems to suggest that the mere passage of a year on the nisab suffices for zakat, which is not true because additional conditions are required. The author defends Al-Hidayah by clarifying that its purpose was only to explain why the hawl is chosen over actual growth as the basis for the ruling, not to state that the hawl alone is sufficient. The additional conditions—thamaniyyah (being gold or silver), sawm (grazing livestock), or trade intention—are mentioned elsewhere in the text. The passage also analogizes to travel licenses, where the cause (travel) replaces the actual hardship. Finally, the commentary elaborates that 'thamaniyyah' refers to gold and silver by nature, excluding coins (fulus) which are prices only by custom. The overall ruling is that zakat is fard once nisab, hawl, and one of these three conditions are met.

Key Terms
حول (hawl): The passage of one lunar year, considered as a proxy for actual growth in wealth.
نماء (nama'): Actual increase or growth of wealth, which is not necessarily required due to hawl being a substitute.
ثمنية (thamaniyyah): The quality of being a price (thaman) by nature, specifically gold and silver.
سوم (sawm): Grazing livestock that are left to pasture for most of the year; zakat applies to them.
نية التجارة (niyyat al-tijarah): Intention of trade when acquiring non-monetary assets, making them zakatable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what additional conditions are required alongside the passage of one year for zakat to be obligatory?
A) Possession of nisab and actual growth
B) Thamaniyyah (gold/silver), sawm (grazing livestock), or trade intention
C) Having the wealth for more than two years
D) Being an adult Muslim

Key Takeaway
The hawl is a proxy for growth, but zakat requires one of three additional conditions: thamaniyyah, sawm, or trade intention.

Understanding the Purpose of al-Hidayah: The Year as Substitute for Growth
Commentary defending al-Hidayah's claim that the year suffices for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of al-Hidayah's statement regarding the year as a substitute for growth and evaluate objections based on missing conditions.

Core Idea
The year substitutes for actual growth, but other conditions are required; al-Hidayah's statement is not deficient but focused.

This passage defends a statement from al-Hidayah that the year (hawl) stands in place of growth (nama'). An objection claimed it omitted other conditions. The commentator clarifies that the statement was never intended to list all conditions; its purpose is to establish that the year suffices as a proxy for growth. Understanding this helps us read classical texts carefully and avoid misinterpreting partial statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The critic argues that al-Hidayah's expression is insufficient because it omits other conditions necessary for zakat (e.g., thamaniyyah, sawm, niyyah al-tijarah).
Recognize that the objection focuses on what the statement does not include.
2
Determine the commentator's response
The commentator responds that al-Hidayah only intended to state that the year replaces growth, not to list all conditions.
The commentator uses the phrase 'لا إلا أن غرض صاحب الهداية من العبارة المذكورة ليس إلا ذكر أن الحول قائم مقام النماء'.
3
Locate the evidence
The commentator points to preceding and subsequent text in al-Hidayah that explicitly mentions the other conditions.
This shows the importance of reading a text in its full context rather than isolating a single phrase.
4
Evaluate the sufficiency
The expression is sufficient for its purpose; no harm if it does not indicate what was not intended.
The commentator says 'ولا بأس بعدم دلالتها على ما لم يقصد منها'.
5
Apply the principle
When reading a classical text, understand the author's intent in context and look for supporting statements elsewhere.
This methodology prevents misreading and hasty criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما في السفر، فإنَّه أقيم مقام المشقة ، فيدارُ الرُّخصةُ عليه سواءٌ وَجَدَ المشقة أم لا، لكن ليس كذلك، بل لا بُدَّ مع الحول من شيء آخر، وهو الثمنية " كما في الثمنين : أي الذهب والفضة، أو السوم كما في الأنعام ، أو نية التجارة في غير ما ذكرنا ولا يخفى على المتدرب أن هذا الإيراد مدفوع بأدنى توجه، فإن غرض صاحب «الهداية» من العبارة المذكورة ليس إلا ذكرُ أنَّ الحول قائم مقامَ النَّماء ، والنَّماء الحقيقي غير معتبر، وأن الحكم دائرٌ على الحول لا على النماء، وهو حاصل منه. وأما كونه مشروطاً بأمر آخر أو غير مشروط فهو بمعزل عنه، وقد دلّ كلام «الهداية» قبل هذه العبارة وبعدها على اشتراط الشروط الآخر التي ذكرها الشارح له كما لا يخفى على من طالعها. فإن قلت : غرض الشارح أنَّ هذه العبارة قاصرة غير وافية. قلت : لا بل هي وافية بما قصد منها ، ولا بأس بعدم دلالتها على ما لم يقصد منها، لا سيما إذا دلَّ عليه كلام سابق أو لاحق.
Just as in travel, for it was placed in the position of hardship, so the dispensation is made dependent on it whether hardship is found or not. But it is not so; rather, along with the year something else is necessary, and that is being a price (thamaniyyah) as in the two prices (gold and silver), or grazing (sawm) as in livestock, or intention of trade in other than what we have mentioned. It is not hidden from the student that this objection is refuted with the slightest attention. For the purpose of the author of al-Hidayah from the mentioned expression is only to state that the year stands in the place of growth, and real growth is not considered, and the ruling revolves around the year, not around growth, and that is achieved from it. As for it being conditional on another matter or unconditional, that is separate from it. Indeed, the words of al-Hidayah before this expression and after it indicate the stipulation of the other conditions that the commentator mentioned, as is not hidden from one who examines it. If you say: The commentator's purpose is that this expression is deficient and insufficient. I say: No, rather it is sufficient for what was intended from it, and there is no harm in it not indicating what was not intended from it, especially if a preceding or subsequent speech indicates it.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiyah) defending al-Hidayah against a critique. The critic argued that al-Hidayah's statement that the year is a substitute for growth is insufficient because it omits other conditions. The commentator responds by clarifying that al-Hidayah only intended to highlight that the year replaces growth, not to list all conditions. The other conditions (thamaniyyah, sawm, niyyah al-tijarah) are stated elsewhere in al-Hidayah. The commentator uses a dialectical style (fa-in qulta… qultu) to refute the objection. The passage demonstrates the need to understand a text within its broader context.

Key Terms
الحول (al-hawl): The passing of one lunar year on the wealth, which is a condition for zakat obligation
النماء (al-nama'): Actual growth or increase of wealth; the year stands in its place for zakat

Three Additional Conditions for Zakat Obligation
Expansion of conditions for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three additional conditions for zakat obligation and determine whether a given type of wealth is subject to zakat based on thamaniyyah, sawm, or trade intention.

Core Idea
Gold and silver are always zakatable; livestock only if grazing; other wealth only if intended for trade.

We know that zakat becomes obligatory when nisab is held for a full lunar year. But the passage clarifies that not all wealth is zakatable even after a year. Three specific conditions—thamaniyyah (being gold or silver by nature), sawm (grazing for most of the year for livestock), and niyyah al-tijarah (intention of trade for other items)—determine whether zakat is due. Additionally, essential needs (hājah aṣliyyah) are exempt. This lesson unpacks each condition and their practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Zakat requires nisab and the passing of one lunar year, but these alone are insufficient. The passage states three additional conditions for obligation.
2
Understand thamaniyyah
Gold and silver are 'price by nature' (thamaniyyah). Zakat is obligatory on them regardless of how they are held, even for personal expenditure. Copper coins (fulus) are not thamaniyyah by nature, so they require trade intention.
The exception 'خلقة' excludes fulus.
3
Understand sawm
For livestock (sheep, cows, camels), they must be 'sā'imah'—grazing for most of the year. If fed at home (علوفة), no zakat is due even if nisab and year are met.
The consideration is for the majority of the year.
4
Understand trade intention
For items other than natural money and grazing livestock, zakat is obligatory only if they are held with the intention of trade. A slave not for service or a house not for dwelling, if held without trade intent, incur no zakat.
If they are for service or dwelling, they are also exempt as basic needs.
5
Apply the basic needs exemption
Essential needs (food, clothing, shelter) are not subject to zakat even if their value exceeds nisab. The hadith of the Prophet storing a year's provision for his family is cited as support.
This is a preventer (mani) of obligation.

[1] His saying: 'Just as in travel' is an analogy for what we are discussing and a support for it. For the dispensations specific to travel were legislated to facilitate the occurrence of hardship in travel, then travel itself was considered as setting up the cause in place of the effect. So whenever travel occurs, the ruling of dispensations is established for the traveler even if hardship is not actually found. [2] His saying: 'But it is not so' means that merely the passing of the year is not sufficient for the obligation of zakat. (3) His saying: 'And it is thamaniyyah... etc.'; its summary: Zakat is not obligatory on wealth even if it reaches the amount of nisab and a year passes over it, except when three things are found: First: thamaniyyah, which is that the wealth is a price by nature (khilqah), meaning it is created to be a price and compensation in contracts and trades, and things are bought with it, and it is gold and silver. Zakat is obligatory on them no matter how they are held, even for expenditure, if a year passes over them and they reach nisab. And he made an exception by his saying 'by nature' because fulus (copper coins) are prices by custom and convention, not by nature. (1) Sawm: from sāmatu tasūmu sawman: meaning grazed. In al-Khāniyyah: al-sā'imah is the grazing animal that suffices with pasture; if it is fed fodder it is 'alūfah, and the consideration is for the majority of the year. It is Kitāb al-Zakāt: Conditions of Zakat. 397: Even if he has a slave not for service, or a house not for dwelling, and he did not intend trade, zakat is not obligatory on them, even if a year passes over them. And it must be surplus to his basic needs, like food and clothing. [2] Second: sawm: it applies to animals that require zakat, like sheep, cows, and camels, as will be mentioned in its place. Linguistically it means grazing. One says shātun sā'imah: a grazing sheep. In legal terminology: it is the animal that suffices with grazing for most of the year. Zakat is obligatory on such animals if they are grazing, but if he feeds them at home and spends on them from his own wealth, there is no zakat on them, even if a year passes and they reach nisab. Third: intention of trade: it applies to other than natural money and livestock. So what is other than these, if it is with the intention of trade, zakat is obligatory on it, otherwise not. [1] His saying: 'not for service' this qualification, and similarly the qualification 'not for dwelling', is only considered to show that the non-obligation of zakat on such a slave and house is due to the lack of trade intention. For if they are for service and dwelling, there is another reason for non-obligation, namely that they are not surplus to basic needs. [2] His saying: 'like food' this and what follows are examples of basic needs. These basic needs are not subject to zakat even if their value reaches nisab. He did not mention the amount of food needed, its type, or its time. Shaykh al-Islam al-Taftazani mentioned that they estimated expenses: bread and condiments according to what is customary, suitable for the husband's wealth and poverty. It is mentioned in al-Muhīt: if he buys food for his sustenance in an amount sufficient for a month or more or less, and it is worth two hundred dirhams, if it is food for a month or less, it is permissible for him to take zakat without dispute, because it is occupied with his basic needs. If it is more, some said it is not permissible and some said it is permissible. Indeed, it is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stored a year's sustenance for his wives. (1) From 'Umar: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to sell the date palms of Banu al-Nadir and reserve for his family their sustenance for a year.' In Sahih al-Bukhari (5:2048) and others.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the conditions for zakat obligation. The commentator begins by comparing the role of the year in zakat to the role of travel in dispensations: just as travel is the cause for dispensations regardless of actual hardship, the year is the cause for zakat regardless of actual growth. However, he clarifies that the year alone is insufficient; three additional conditions are needed. First, thamaniyyah: the wealth must be gold or silver by nature (khilqah), not merely by custom (like copper coins). Second, sawm: for livestock, they must be grazing for most of the year. Third, niyyah al-tijarah: for other items, intention of trade is required. The commentator also discusses the exemption for basic needs (hājah aṣliyyah): items like food and clothing necessary for living are not subject to zakat even if their value exceeds nisab, because they are not surplus. A hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari is cited to support that storing a year's worth of food is permissible and does not negate eligibility for zakat.

Key Terms
الثمنية (al-thamaniyyah): The quality of being a price by nature, i.e., gold and silver, which are created as mediums of exchange
السوم (al-sawm): The condition that livestock are grazing freely for most of the year, not fed by the owner
نية التجارة (niyyah al-tijarah): The intention of trade, which makes merchandise other than gold/silver and livestock subject to zakat
الحاجة الأصلية (al-hājah al-aṣliyyah): Essential needs such as food, clothing, and shelter that are exempt from zakat

Key Takeaway
Zakat obligation requires not just nisab and a year, but also that the wealth meets one of three conditions: being gold/silver by nature, grazing livestock, or trade goods—and must be surplus to basic needs.

Three Conditions for Zakat: Surplus, Pasturing, and Trade Intention
Listing of three conditions for zakat with initial commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for zakat and apply them to identify which assets are zakatable.

Core Idea
Zakat is not due on all wealth; only on surplus that is actively growing: pastured livestock, trade goods, and assets beyond basic needs.

Zakat is fard on specific categories of wealth. The Hanafi school conditions zakatability on three key criteria: the wealth must be surplus to basic needs, livestock must be pastured, and other goods must be intended for trade. This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya lists these conditions and clarifies their application through examples and scholarly comments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Conditions
Read the passage and list the three conditions explicitly mentioned: surplus to basic need (fadl an al-hajah al-asliyyah), pasturing (al-sawm), and intention of trade (niyyat al-tijarah).
These are sequential: first condition applies to all assets, second to livestock, third to other trade goods.
2
Understand the First Condition: Surplus to Basic Need
Analyze what counts as basic need: food, clothing, shelter, and tools of trade. The passage gives examples and notes that even if such assets equal nisab, no zakat is due. Note the discussion about storing food for a year from al-Muhit.
The Prophet (PBUH) stored a year’s food, indicating long-term storage for basic need is exempt.
3
Analyze the Second Condition: Pasturing
Define 'sawm' linguistically and legally: animals that are self-sufficient through grazing for most of the year. Zakat is due on such pastured livestock reaching nisab; but if fed at home, no zakat even if nisab and a year pass.
This applies only to livestock categories where zakat is legislated (sheep, cows, camels).
4
Examine the Third Condition: Trade Intention
Intention of trade is required for zakatability of assets other than natural metals (gold/silver) and livestock. If a slave or house is owned without trade intention, no zakat. The commentary clarifies that the conditions of 'not for service' and 'not for residence' highlight that if they are for personal use, they are excluded by both trade intention and surplus condition.
Trade intention must be present at acquisition or during the year (later Hanafi detail).

حتى لو كان له عبد لا للخدمة ، أو دار لا للسكنى، ولم ينو التجارة لا تجب فيهما الزَّكاة، وإن حال عليهما الحول. ولا بد أن يكون فاضلاً عن حاجته الأصلية كالأطعمة، والنياب [؟]
وثانيها : السوم ؛ وهو في الدواب التي تجب فيها الزَّكاةُ كالغنم والبقر والإبل على ما سيأتي ذكره في موضعه وهو عبارة لغة عن الرعي، يقال شاة سائمة : أي راعية وفي اصطلاح الشرع: هي المكتفية بالرعي في أكثر السنة، فتلزم الدواب الزَّكاةَ إذا كانت سائمة، وإن كان يعلفها في بيته ويصرف عليها من عنده فلا زكاة عليها، وإن مضت عليه السنة وبلغت نصاباً.
وثالثها : نيَّة التّجارة ؛ وهو في غير الثَّمن الخلقي والدواب، فما عداها إذا كانت بنية التجارة تجب فيه الزكاة وإلا فلا.
[ ١ ] قوله : لا للخدمة هذا القيد، وكذا قيد لا للسكنى» إنّما اعتبر ليظهر أنَّ عدم وجوب الزكاة في مثل هذا العبد والدار إنما هو لعدم نية التجارة، فإنّه إن كان للخدمة والسكني فلعدم وجوبها فيهما وجه آخر ، وهو كونهما غير فاضلين عن الحاجة الأصلية.
[٢]قوله : كالأطعمة؛ هذا وما بعده مثال للحاجة الأصلية، فهذه الحوائج الأصلية لا تجب فيها الزكاة وإن بلغت قيمتها نصاباً ، ولم يذكر مقدار الطعام المحتاج إليه وجنسه وزمانه ، وذكر شيخ الإسلام التفتازاني أنهم قدروا في النفقة الخبز والإدام بالمعروف المناسب ليسار الزوج وعساره.
وقد ذكر في «المحيط»: أنه إذا اشترى طعاماً لقوته مقدار ما يكفي شهراً أو أكثر أو أقل، وهو يساوي مائتي درهم إن كان قوت شهر أو أقل حل له أخذ الزكاة بلا خلاف ؛ لأنه مشغول بحاجته الأصليّة، وإن كان أكثر قال بعضهم : لا يحلّ، وقال بعضهم : يحلّ ، فقد صح أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ادخر لنسائه قوت سنة (١).
The Book of Zakat: Conditions of Zakat. Even if he has a slave not for service, or a house not for residence, and he did not intend trade, zakat is not obligatory on them, even if a year passes over them. And it must be surplus to his basic need, like foodstuffs, and [clothing?]. Secondly: Pasturing; it applies to animals on which zakat is due like sheep, cows, and camels as will be mentioned in its place. It is linguistically grazing; it is said a pasturing sheep: i.e., grazing. In legal terminology: it is the animal that is self-sufficient through grazing for most of the year. So zakat is obligatory on animals when they are pasturing, but if he feeds them at home and spends on them from his own wealth, there is no zakat on them, even if a year passes and they reach the nisab. Thirdly: Intention of trade; it applies to other than natural metals and livestock. So besides those, if they are with intention of trade, zakat is obligatory; otherwise not. [1] His saying: 'not for service' and similarly the condition 'not for residence' is considered only to show that the absence of zakat on such a slave and house is due to the absence of trade intention. For if they were for service and residence, there is another reason for the absence of obligation, i.e., they are not surplus to basic need. [2] His saying: 'like foodstuffs'; this and what follows are examples of basic need. So these basic needs are subject to no zakat even if their value reaches the nisab. He did not mention the quantity, type, or time of the needed food. Shaykh al-Islam al-Taftazani mentioned that they estimated for maintenance bread and oil according to custom appropriate to the husband's wealth and poverty. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit: if he buys food for his sustenance sufficient for a month or more or less, and it is worth two hundred dirhams, if it is sustenance for a month or less, it is permissible for him to take zakat without dispute, because he is occupied with his basic need. If it is more, some said it is not permissible, and some said it is permissible. It has been authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stored for his wives a year's sustenance.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya lists the three conditions for zakat as per the Hanafi school. First condition: The wealth must be surplus to the owner's basic needs such as food, clothing, and shelter. Even if a slave or house is owned for a full year, no zakat is due if they are not intended for trade and are used for personal service or residence. Second condition: For grazing livestock, they must be pastured (sa'imah) for most of the year. Animals fed at home are exempt. Third condition: For other goods, there must be an intention of trade at the time of acquisition. The commentary explains that the examples of food highlight that basic provisions are exempt even if they accumulate. The dispute from al-Muhit about storing food beyond a year's supply shows that some scholars allow zakat exemption for larger stores, citing the Prophet's practice of storing a year's food.

Key Terms
السوم (al-sawm): In legal terminology, it refers to livestock that are self-sufficient through grazing for most of the year.
نية التجارة (niyyat al-tijarah): The intention of trade when acquiring an asset, making it subject to zakat.
الحاجة الأصلية (al-hajah al-asliyyah): Basic necessities such as food, clothing, shelter, and tools of trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the condition for zakat on livestock?
A) They must be owned for a full year.
B) They must be both pasturing and intended for trade.
C) They must be pasturing (sa'imah).
D) They must be fed at home by the owner.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is only due on wealth that is surplus to basic needs; livestock must be pastured; other goods must be intended for trade.

Basic Needs Exemption in Zakat: Refining the Examples
Refining examples of basic needs exemption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of basic needs exemption and apply it to determine whether an asset acquired for trade but used for personal needs is subject to zakat.

Core Idea
Wealth genuinely needed for survival is never zakatable, even if deliberately bought for trade.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya addresses objections to listing food, houses, weapons, tools, and books as basic needs exempt from zakat. It clarifies that the key factor is the owner's genuine need, not the initial intention of purchase. We'll walk through the objections and the Hanafi responses to refine our understanding of the exemption.

Guided Path
1
State the basic needs exemption principle
Identify the Hanafi rule: wealth that is a basic necessity (al-hajah al-asliyyah) is exempt from zakat, even if acquired with trade intention, provided it is actually used for basic living.
This principle overrides the usual condition of growth (nama') for zakatability.
2
Identify the objection to food as an example
The objector argues: if food has not had a year pass, no zakat anyway; if a year has passed, it is no longer a basic need (since it would have been consumed). So food is not a valid example of a basic need exempt from zakat.
The objection relies on the assumption that surplus food after a year is not needed.
3
Analyze the response: need overrides trade intention
The response explains that food may be bought for trade but then consumed gradually over the year for the family's needs. At year-end, the remaining food is still a basic need because it is still being used. Similarly, a house bought for trade but used for residence is exempt.
The key is actual need, not initial intention.
4
Evaluate the defense for weapons and books
The commentator adds qualifiers like 'weapons that one uses' and 'books for their people' to emphasize that these items are exempt only when they fulfill a basic need (e.g., self-defense or learning). Without the qualifier, the objection would claim redundancy.
The defense shows that the qualifier is not redundant but clarifies the basis of exemption.
5
Conclude the refinement: surplus vs. need
The passage concludes that books are never zakatable because they are not growth assets; the qualifier 'for their people' only affects eligibility to receive zakat, not the obligation to pay it.
This distinction highlights that different categories of assets have different rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأثاث المنزل، ودواب الركوب، وعبيد الخدمة، ودور السكني، وسلاح يستعملها، وآلات المحترفة، والكتب لأهلها
ثم أورد على الشارح في تمثيله بالأطعمة أنَّ الأطعمة إن لم يحلّ عليها الحولُ فلا زكاة فيها ؛ لفقدان الحول، وإن حال الحولُ فهي فارغة عن الحوائج الأصلية، فلا يصح التمثيل بها. وأجيب عنه : بأنه يحتمل أن يشتري الطَّعامَ بنيَّة التجارة ويكون محتاجاً إليها بنفسه وعياله، فيصرف على عياله إلى آخرِ السَّنة، ويبقى الطّعام، فلا زكاة فيه، وهكذا حالُ دار اشتراها بنية التجارة وهو محتاج إليها للسكنى. ونحوها.
(1) قوله : وأثاث ، بالفتح : أي متاع بيته من ظروف الشرب والأكل والطبخ
[٢]قوله : يستعملها ؛ فيه أنه قيد مستدرك ؛ لأنَّ الأسلحة إن لم تكن للتجارة فلا زكاة فيها لعدم النماء، وإلا ففيها الزَّكاة. ويجاب عنه : بأن فيها القيد لإفادة أنَّ مَن يحتاجُ إلى استعمالها كالغزاة والمحاربين وغيرهم لا زكاة في أسلحتهم ؛ لعدم فراغها عن الحاجة الأصلية، وإن كان اشتراها بنية التجارة.
[٣] قوله : وآلات المحترفة ؛ أي المحتاجُ إليها في الحرفة مثل قدور الطباخين والصباغين، وآلات النجارين
[٤] قوله : لأهلها ؛ أي من يحتاجُ إليها لتعليم، أو تدريس ، أو تعلم، أو تصحيح، وغير ذلك، ويرد عليه بأنه مستدرك ؛ لأنها لو لم تكن للتجارة لا تجب فيها الزكاة، وإن لم تكن عند أهلها وإن كانت بنيَّة التّجارة تجب، وإن كانت عند أهلها
(١) التقييد بأهلها غير معتبر المفهوم إلا أنه يراد به إخراجها عن حاجته الأصلية، فالكتب لا زكاة فيها على الأهل وغيرهم من أي علم كانت لكونها غير نامية، وإنما الفرق بين الأهل وغيرهم في جواز أخذ الزكاة والمنع عنه فمن كان من أهلها إذا كان محتاجاً إليها للتدريس والحفظ والتصحيح، فإنه لا يخرج بها عن الفقر فله أخذ الزكاة، وتمامه في رد المحتار (٢ : ٨)، وينظر : ((البحر» (٢ : ٢٢٢).
And household furnishings, riding animals, service slaves, residences, weapons that one uses, tools of craftsmen, and books for their people. Then an objection was raised against the commentator regarding his example of food: that food, if a year does not pass over it, there is no zakat on it due to the absence of the year; and if a year passes, it is devoid of basic needs, so the example is invalid. And it was answered: It is possible that he buys food with the intention of trade and needs it for himself and his family, then he spends on his family until the end of the year, and the food remains, so no zakat is due on it. Similarly, the case of a house he bought with trade intention while needing it for residence, and similar cases. (1) His saying: 'furnishings' (athath) means household goods like drinking, eating, and cooking vessels. [2] His saying: 'weapons that one uses' is objected to as redundant because if weapons are not for trade, no zakat is due due to lack of growth; otherwise zakat is due. It is answered: The condition is added to indicate that those who need to use them, such as warriors and combatants and others, have no zakat on their weapons due to their not being surplus to basic need, even if he bought them with trade intention. [3] His saying: 'tools of craftsmen' means those needed for the craft, like the pots of cooks and dyers, and the tools of carpenters. [4] His saying: 'books for their people' means those who need them for teaching, instructing, learning, correcting, etc. It is objected that this is redundant because if they are not for trade, no zakat is due, and if they are for trade, zakat is due even if they are with their people. (1) The qualification with 'their people' is not considered in terms of its apparent meaning, but rather it is intended to exclude them from basic needs. Books have no zakat on them for their people or others, regardless of the field of knowledge, because they are not growth assets. The difference between their people and others is only in permissibility of taking zakat and its prohibition. So one who is a scholar and needs them for teaching, memorization, and correction, he does not exit poverty due to them, so he may take zakat. The full discussion is in Radd al-Muhtar (2:8) and see al-Bahr (2:222).
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This section from 'Umda al-Ri'aya addresses objections to the previous examples of basic needs. An objector argued that using food as an example is invalid because if a year hasn't passed, no zakat anyway; if a year has passed, it's no longer needed. The answer is that food may be bought for trade and then consumed gradually, so it remains exempt due to need. Similarly, a house bought for trade but used for residence is exempt. The commentary then critiques and defends the author's inclusion of qualifiers like 'weapons that one uses' and 'books for their people.' The defense is that these qualifiers remove items from being surplus to basic need, thus exempting them from zakat. The final note clarifies that books are never subject to zakat regardless of ownership because they are not growth assets; the qualifier distinguishes who may receive zakat.

Key Terms
الحاجة الأصلية (al-hajah al-asliyyah): Basic necessities that exempt wealth from zakat, even if acquired for trade but actually needed.
أثاث (athath): Household furnishings including vessels for drinking, eating, and cooking.
آلات المحترفة (alat al-muhtarifah): Tools of craftsmen needed for their profession, such as pots for cooks and tools for carpenters.

C) Because they are used for trade.
D) Because the scholar is poor.

Key Takeaway
Genuine basic need overrides trade intention in determining zakat liability, and certain assets like books are categorically exempt because they lack growth potential.

Exempt Property in Zakat: Household Items, Tools, and Books
Lists exempt property with commentary on objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the categories of property exempt from zakat and explain the principle of al-hajat al-asaliyyah (basic needs) that underlies their exemption.

Core Idea
Zakat is not due on assets used for basic needs, even if acquired with trade intention.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam, but not every asset is subject to it. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi rule that property essential for daily life and profession is exempt. The passage lists specific categories and clarifies common objections, reinforcing the principle that necessity overrides potential liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed categories
Scan the passage and enumerate the seven types of exempt property: household furnishings, riding animals, servants for service, residential houses, weapons, tools of trade, and books for their owners.
Each category shares the trait of being used for basic needs.
2
Understand the underlying principle
Note that zakat is waived because these items are considered 'hajat asaliyyah' (basic needs) and are not growth-oriented (ghayr namiyah).
Growth potential (nama') is a key condition for zakat on wealth.
3
Examine the objections and responses
The passage addresses objections about food and weapons. For food, even if bought for trade, if consumed for family needs during the year, the remaining stock is exempt. For weapons, even if bought for trade, if needed for defense, they are exempt.
The qualification 'that he uses' (yasta'miluha) is not superfluous but emphasizes ongoing need.
4
Apply the rule to books
Books are exempt for all because they are not growth assets. The difference between scholars and others is only in receiving zakat: a scholar in need of books may still receive zakat because the books do not make him rich.
The phrase 'for their owners' is not a condition for exemption but clarifies the owner's need.
5
Distinguish from trade goods
If an item is bought for trade but actually used for basic needs, it remains exempt. The key is actual usage, not initial intention.
A car bought for Uber but also used for personal errands: exemption depends on the extent of personal use.

And household furnishings, riding animals, servants for service, residential houses, weapons that he uses, tools of the trade, and books for their owners. Then [the commentator] was objected to regarding his example with foods that if the year has not passed on the foods, there is no zakat on them due to lack of the year, and if the year has passed, they are free from basic needs, so the example is not valid. And it was answered: that it is possible that he bought the food with the intention of trade and is in need of it for himself and his family, so he spends on his family until the end of the year, and the food remains, so there is no zakat on it, and similarly the case of a house he bought with the intention of trade while he is in need of it for residence, and similar things. His saying: 'and tools of the trade' meaning what is needed in the trade like pots of cooks and dyers, and tools of carpenters. His saying: 'for their owners' meaning those who need them for teaching, or instructing, or learning, or correcting, and other things. The qualification 'for their owners' is not considered in terms of concept, rather it is intended to remove them from basic need. So books have no zakat on them for the owners and others, whatever field they are, because they are not growing. The difference between the owners and others is only concerning the permissibility of taking zakat and its prohibition. So whoever is among the owners, if he is in need of them for teaching, memorization, and correction, he does not thereby exit from poverty, so he may take zakat. The completion is in Radd al-Muhtar (2:8) and see al-Bahr (2:222).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing items that are exempt from zakat due to being essential for daily life. The author enumerates: household furnishings (like utensils), riding animals, servants for service, residential houses, weapons that one uses, tools of trade (e.g., pots for cooks, tools for carpenters), and books for their owners (scholars who need them for teaching, learning, etc.). A commentator then addresses an objection regarding an example using food: if food is bought for trade but the owner is also in need of it for his family, he may consume it throughout the year, and what remains at year-end is not subject to zakat because it is used for basic needs. Similarly, a house bought for trade but needed for residence is exempt. The commentator then clarifies that the qualification 'that he uses' for weapons is not superfluous; even if bought for trade, if the owner needs them for combat or defense, they are exempt. For books, the exemption applies to all, not just scholars, because books are not growth-oriented assets. The only difference between scholars and others is that scholars may still receive zakat even if they own books, because the books are considered a basic need for their profession. The passage relies on the principle that assets used for basic necessities are not subject to zakat, even if acquired with trade intention, as long as the need persists.

Key Terms
أثاث المنزل (athāth al-manzil): Household furnishings and utensils used for everyday life, such as vessels for drinking, eating, and cooking.
آلات المحترفة (ālāt al-muhtarifah): Tools of the trade that one needs for his profession, such as pots for cooks, tools for carpenters, etc.
حاجة أصلية (hājah asaliyyah): Basic need; an essential requirement for daily living or professional work that renders an asset exempt from zakat.

Key Takeaway
Property used for basic needs—household items, tools, books, and similar—is exempt from zakat, even if acquired with trade intention, as long as the need persists.
