Rules for the Zakat Collector and Merging Acquired Wealth
Rules for the zakat collector regarding quality selection and merging mid-year acquisitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for the zakat collector regarding taking the middle quality and handling missing ages, and apply the rule for merging mid-year acquisitions to a nisab.

Core Idea
The zakat collector must take the middle quality; missing exact age allows a lower or higher age with adjustment.

This lesson explains the duties of the official zakat collector (al-muṣaddiq) in assessing and collecting livestock zakat. The primary rule is that he must take the middle quality, neither the best nor the worst, to balance the rights of the owner and the poor. If the exact prescribed age is unavailable, he has flexibility: he can take a lower age and collect extra payment, or take a higher age and refund the difference. Additionally, any wealth acquired during the zakat year is merged with existing nisab for calculation. These rules ensure fairness and practicality in zakat collection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
State that the collector must take only the middle quality (al-wasaṭ) of livestock. Understand what 'middle' means: not the best, not the worst, defined as the highest of the low and lowest of the high, determined by average value.
The hadith prohibits taking the best assets, emphasizing mercy to the owner.
2
Analyze the exception for missing age
If the exact required age (e.g., bint labun) is not available, the collector may take a lower age and require additional payment (al-adnā maʿa al-faḍl) or take a higher age and refund the surplus (al-aʿlā wa yaruddu al-faḍl). Trace the logic: this prevents hardship and ensures the collector does not overcharge or undercollect.
This is a practical solution when the exact age is scarce.
3
Apply the rule of merging acquired wealth
When an owner acquires additional wealth of the same type (e.g., dirhams) mid-year, it is merged with the existing nisab for zakat purposes. For example, if someone has 200 dirhams for a full year and acquires 100 more mid-year, the total 300 is treated as a single nisab and zakat is due on the whole.
The merger occurs regardless of when the acquisition happens (beginning, middle, or end of the year).
4
Locate the dalil and its implication
The hadith from Jarīr ibn Ḥāzim (in Sunan al-Bayhaqī) shows the collector preferring to leave the best animals and take from the 'boundaries' (ḥawāshī). This supports the rule of taking middle quality and avoiding the best.
The ḥadīth is aḥad (single transmission), hence zannī in both thubūt and dalāla, but it is accepted by the Hanafī school.

The collector takes only the middle. And if he does not find the required age, he takes the lower with extra, or the higher, and refunds the extra. And acquired [wealth] is merged mid-hawl in its ruling to the nisab of its type: i.e., if he had two hundred dirhams and a year had passed on them, and he acquired another hundred dirhams mid-year, he adds the hundred to the two hundred.
(1) His saying: 'al-musaddiq' – active participle from the form taf'il; he is the taker of sadaqah and the agent for its collection on behalf of the imam.
(2) His saying: 'except the middle' – meaning he does not take the best of the people's wealth, nor the worst, observing both sides. And the prophetic prohibition against taking other than the middle has been reported in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and others.
[3] His saying: 'and if he does not find...' – for example, if the wajib is a bint labun and he finds only a bint makhad, he takes it with extra; and in the opposite case he takes it and refunds the extra to the owner.
(4) His saying: 'is merged' – passive voice, meaning the owner merges it and pays zakat on it together with the nisab.
[0] His saying: 'middle...' – what is meant is before the end of the year, whether it be middle, end, or beginning.
[6] His saying: 'is merged...' – know that acquired wealth is of two types:
(1) al-musaddiq: he is the taker of sadaqah on behalf of the imam, so he takes the rights from camels and sheep. See: al-Lisan (2419).
(2) al-wasat: it is the highest of the low and the lowest of the high. It is said: if there are twenty sheep (da'n) and twenty goats (ma'z), he takes the middle; its knowledge is that he values the middle of the goats and sheep, so a sheep is taken that equals half the value of each. See: Ghunyat Dhawi al-Ahkam (1:178) and al-Durr al-Mukhtar (2:22).
(3) From Jarir ibn Hazim: the collector of sadaqah said, 'By Allah, what I have left is more beloved to me than what I came with. Go, return it to them and take their sadaqat from the boundaries of their wealth.' In Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir (4:101) and others.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rules for the zakat collector (al-musaddiq) appointed by the imam. It contains four key rulings: (1) The collector must take the middle quality of the livestock, avoiding the best and the worst, as per prophetic command. (2) If the exact age required (e.g., a bint labun) is not available, he may take a lower age and collect extra payment from the owner, or take a higher age and refund the difference. (3) Newly acquired property (al-mustafād) acquired mid-year is merged with the existing nisab for zakat purposes; the example given is adding 100 dirhams to an existing 200 upon which a year has passed. (4) The definitions of key terms: al-musaddiq is the collector, al-wasat is the middle quality, and the method of determining the middle when both sheep and goats are present is by estimating value. Footnotes reference the hadith prohibiting taking other than the middle, and a narration from Jarir ibn Hazim illustrating the principle.

Key Terms
المصدق (al-muṣaddiq): The official appointed by the imam to collect zakat from the people.
الوسط (al-wasaṭ): The medium quality of livestock, not the best nor the worst.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The zakat collector must take the middle quality; if the prescribed age is lacking, he may take a lower age with extra payment or a higher age with a refund, and newly acquired wealth is merged with existing nisab for zakat calculation.

The Zakat Collector Takes the Middle and Missing Age Rule
Ruling with hadith proof on collector's duty and handling missing age

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings regarding the zakat collector's duty (taking middle quality and handling missing age) and identify the hadith proof that supports them.

Core Idea
The zakat collector must take middle-quality livestock; if the exact age is missing, a near age with compensation is taken.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains two practical rulings for the zakat collector. First, he must take animals of middle quality—neither the best nor the worst—to balance the rights of the owner and the poor. Second, if the precise required age of camel is unavailable, he takes the nearest age either lower with a supplement from the owner or higher with a refund to the owner. The proof is a prophetic hadith reported in Sunan al-Bayhaqi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and list the two distinct obligations: (a) the collector must take the middle quality, (b) if the required age is missing, take a near age with compensation.
These are separate but related: quality and age.
2
Locate the hadith proof
Find the hadith cited from al-Bayhaqi via Jarir ibn Hazim. Note that the collector's words imply prohibition of taking the best and instruction to take from 'outer parts' (i.e., middle).
The hadith is ahad, but accepted in practice.
3
Understand the legal cause (illa)
Reflect on why the middle is chosen: it avoids harming the owner (by taking the best) and avoids cheating the poor (by taking the worst). The missing age rule ensures the obligation is fulfilled practically.
The principle is 'observing both sides' (ri'ayat al-janibayn).
4
Apply the missing age rule
Work through the example: if bint labun is required but only bint makhad is available, the collector takes bint makhad plus a supplement (e.g., two sheep or cash value). In reverse, he takes the higher age and refunds the excess.
The compensation must be just and agreed upon.

Source Text

(۱) قوله : المصدق ؛ اسم فاعل من باب التفعيل، وهو آخذ الصدقة والعامل لتحصيلها من جانب الإمام. (٢) قوله : إلا الوسط ؛ أي لا يأخذ عمدة أموال أرباب الأموال، ولا أرذلها رعاية للجانبين ، وقد ورد النَّهيُّ النَّبوي عن أخذِ غير الوسط في «سنن البيهقي» وغيره. عن جرير بن حازم قال الساعي الصدقة : والله للذي تركت أحب إلي من الذي جئت به اذهب فردها عليهم وخذ صدقاتهم من حواشي أموالهم» في «سنن البيهقي الكبير» (٤ : ١٠١)، وغيره. Commentary
This passage states two rulings: (1) The zakat collector appointed by the imam must take animals of middle quality—neither the best nor the worst. This is based on a prophetic hadith commanding avoidance of extremes. (2) If the exact age of camel required for zakat (e.g., bint labun) is not available, the collector takes the nearest age either lower (with a cash/animal supplement from the owner) or higher (and refunds the excess to the owner). The commentary clarifies the terms and provides examples.

الوسط (al-wasat): The middle quality of livestock—not the best nor the worst.

Paying Cash for Zakat on Land Produce
Ruling with proof for paying cash value for 'ushr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying cash for 'ushr and explain the istihsan-based proof that allows it.

Core Idea
Paying cash for 'ushr is allowed because the purpose is feeding the poor, which cash achieves equally.

This short passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a practical question: must zakat on land produce be paid in the actual crop, or can the owner pay its cash value? The Hanafi answer permits cash, based on a deep look at the objective of zakat. We'll examine the reasoning and the cross-madhhab debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the text to determine what the land owner is permitted to do. The text states he may pay one-tenth of the crop or its value.
The ruling is permissibility (ja'iz), not obligation.
2
Extract the Proof
Locate the reasoning: 'because the command to give zakat is for delivering sustenance to the poor.' This is a teleological argument (ta'lil) using the purpose of the law.
The proof is not a direct text but an inference from the objective.
3
Classify the Proof as Istihsan
Understand that this is istihsan (juridical preference): setting aside a qiyas (in-kind only) for a stronger consideration—here, the overall objective of zakat.
Istihsan is a key Hanafi method for expanding rulings.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i Position
Note that the Shafi'i school generally requires in-kind payment for 'ushr, citing textual literalism. This shows a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi view is based on maqasid (objectives); the Shafi'i on the apparent meaning of texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأرض يدفعُ عشرَ ما خرج أو قيمته ; وذلك لأنَّ الأمر بأداء الزَّكاة إلى الفقير؛ لأجل إيصال الرِّزْقِ إلى الفقراء، ويستوي فيه العين وقيمته، ولم يوجد دليل يمنع أداء القيمة.
The land gives one-tenth of what comes out (produce) or its value. That is because the command to give zakat to the poor is for the sake of delivering sustenance to the poor, and the actual goods and their value are equal in this, and there is no evidence that prevents paying the value.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage states that when paying zakat on agricultural produce ('ushr), the owner may pay either one-tenth of the actual crop or its cash equivalent. The reason is that the objective of zakat is to provide for the poor, which is achieved equally by goods or cash. Since no text prohibits paying value, it is permissible. This is a Hanafi position that allows cash payments for zakat in some cases.

Key Terms
القيمة (al-qimah): Cash or monetary value equivalent to the one-tenth share.
تعليل (ta'lil): Legal reasoning based on the underlying purpose or cause of a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is paying cash for 'ushr permissible?
A) Because the poor prefer cash.
B) Because the command is for delivering sustenance, and cash is equal to goods in that.
C) Because the farmer may choose any method.
D) Because there is a direct hadith allowing cash.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, paying cash for 'ushr is permissible because the purpose of zakat is delivering benefit to the poor, which cash achieves equally to goods.

Adding Acquired Wealth (Mustafad) to Nisab: Types and Dispute
Ruling and ikhtilaf on zakat for wealth acquired mid-year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify acquired wealth (mustafad) by type and origin, apply the Hanafi rule for adding it to the nisab, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-evidence.

Core Idea
Acquired wealth of the same type as the nisab is added to the original year; different types start a new year.

A person already possessing a nisab may acquire more wealth during the year. Is that new wealth subject to zakat immediately, or does it require its own year? This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the Hanafi position, which distinguishes by type (jins) and origin (offspring vs. purchase/inheritance), and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view based on a weak hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on adding mustafad
State that the Hanafi school holds that acquired wealth of the same type (jins) as the existing nisab is added to it, and zakat is due on the total at the end of the original year.
2
Distinguish the types of mustafad
Classify mustafad into same jins vs. different jins. Within same jins, separate offspring (consensus) from other acquisitions (purchase/inheritance, which is disputed).
Different jins: e.g., acquiring cattle while having camel nisab – no addition by consensus.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and its dalil
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that newly acquired wealth requires its own full year, citing the hadith: 'Whoever acquires wealth, no zakat is due on it until a year passes.'
The hadith is narrated by Tirmidhi with a weak chain.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
Explain that the Hanafis consider the hadith weak (sahif) and interpret it as referring to wealth of a different type, not the same type. Thus, it does not conflict with the Hanafi rule.
This interpretation is verified in Fath al-Qadir.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Describe the real-world difference: Under Hanafi, zakat on purchased camels is due at the end of the original year; under Shafi'i, a separate year begins for the purchased camels.

[٤] قوله : يُضمّ ; بصيغة المجهول، أي يضمُّهُ المالك، ويزكيه مع النصاب. [0]قوله : وسط ... الخ ; المراد به ما قبل انقضاء الحول وسطاً كان أو آخراً أو أوَّلاً. [٦] قوله : يضم...الخ ; اعلم أنَّ المستفاد على نوعين : أحدهما : أن يكون من جنس النصاب الذي عنده، كما إذا كانت له إبل فاستفادَ إبلاً في أثناء الحول. وثانيهما : أن يكون من غير جنسه كما إذا استفاد بقراً في صورة نصاب الإبل، وهذا لا ضمّ فيه اتفاقاً، بل يستأنف للمستفاد حساب آخر. والأول على نوعين : أحدهما : أن يكون المستفاد من الأصل؛ كالأرواح والأولاد، وهذا يُضَمُ إجماعاً. والثاني : أن يكون مستفاداً بسبب آخر ; كالمشتري والمورث، وهذا يُضم عندنا خلافاً للشافعي له، له حديث: «من استفاد مالاً فلا زكاة عليه حتى يحول عليه الحول» (۲) ، أخرجه الترمذي بسند ضعيف ، وهو عندنا محمول على تخالف الجنس، كما حققه في «فتح القدير» (۳).

[4] He said: 'is added' in the passive, meaning the owner adds it and pays zakat on it with the nisab. [0] He said: 'middle of the year' means before the end of the year, whether middle, beginning, or end. [6] He said: 'adds' know that acquired wealth is of two types: one: that it is of the same type as the nisab he has, e.g., he has camels and acquires more camels during the year. Second: that it is of a different type, e.g., he acquires cattle while having a camel nisab; this is not added by consensus, but a separate calculation is started. The first type is of two kinds: one: that the acquired is from the original, e.g., offspring and young; this is added by consensus. Second: that it is acquired by another cause, e.g., purchase or inheritance; this is added in our school contrary to al-Shafi'i, who has a hadith: 'Whoever acquires wealth, no zakat is due on it until a year passes' (Tirmidhi, weak). And his statement: 'in its ruling' means in the ruling of the acquired, which is the obligation of zakat, i.e., the year that passed on the original is considered for the acquired; and it is possible that the pronoun refers to the year. [1] He said: 'to the year' so the meaning is 'in the ruling of the year,' which is the obligation of zakat.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage explains the rule for zakat on wealth acquired during the zakat year. When a person already possesses a nisab and acquires more of the same type (e.g., more camels), the acquired wealth is added to the original nisab and zakat is paid on the total at the end of the original year. If the acquired is of a different type, it is not added; a separate year starts. Within the same type, offspring are added by consensus, but wealth from purchase or inheritance is added according to the Hanafi school, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The Shafi'i proof is a weak hadith that requires a full year for new wealth; Hanafis interpret that hadith as referring to wealth of a different type. The commentary clarifies the meaning of 'in its ruling'.

Key Terms
المستفاد (al-mustafad): Wealth acquired after the zakat year has started, e.g., by purchase, inheritance, or birth.
يضم (yudamm): Adding the newly acquired wealth to the existing nisab for zakat calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is added by consensus, like offspring.
C) It is added only if the purchaser intended to add it.
D) It is added in the Hanafi school, contrary to Shafi'i.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, acquired wealth of the same type as the existing nisab is added to it for zakat, unless it is from a different type which starts a new year.

Zakat on Nisab Only – The Afw Exemption
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for livestock surplus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on zakat for livestock surplus and explain the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar.

Core Idea
Zakat on livestock applies only to the full nisab; the surplus between nisabs is exempt (afw).

When a person owns livestock that exceeds one nisab but does not reach the next, does zakat fall on the entire herd or only on the minimum nisab? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, which distinguishes between the nisab and the afw (surplus). Understanding this distinction prevents overpayment of zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab and afw in the scenario
Look at the example in the text: 35 camels. The first nisab for camels is 25. The surplus (afw) is the 10 camels between 25 and 36 (the next nisab). The text states that zakat is due only on the nisab of 25.
The afw is defined as 'what is between two nisabs'.
2
Apply the rule of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
According to these two imams, zakat is wajib on the nisab portion only. For 35 camels, only one bint makhad is due (from the first 25). The extra 10 camels (afw) do not increase the zakat obligation.
They support this with the example: if 10 camels die after the year, the obligation remains unchanged, because the nisab (25) is still intact.
3
Apply the opposing view of Muhammad and Zufar
Muhammad and Zufar hold that the entire herd (nisab + afw) is considered together. For 35 camels, they would likely require additional zakat beyond one bint makhad, though the exact calculation is not detailed here.
Their reasoning considers the total number as a single unit for zakat.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, a person with 35 camels for one full year pays only one bint makhad. Under Muhammad/Zufar, the same person would pay more (e.g., two bint makhad or equivalent). This difference directly affects the amount of zakat due.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[٢] قوله : وهو بنتُ مخاض ; الواجبة من خمس وعشرين إلى خمس وثلاثين. [٣] قوله : كان الواجب على حاله ; فيجب أداء بنت مخاض ; لبقاء النصاب وهلاك العفو، وهو ما بين النصابين لا يسقط منه شيئاً، هذا عندهما. (۱) العفو وهو ما بين النصابين، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، وقال محمد وزفر : مجموع النصاب والعفو ينظر : فتح باب العناية» (١ : ٥٠٥).
And zakat is on the nisab, not on the afw (surplus). For if he owns 35 camels, the obligatory (bint makhad) is only on 25, not on the total; even if 10 perish after the year, the obligation remains as it was. [2] He said: 'and it is bint makhad' due from 25 to 35. [3] He said: 'the obligation remains as it was' so paying bint makhad is obligatory because the nisab remains and the afw is destroyed; it (the afw) is what is between the two nisabs and nothing of it falls (from the obligation). This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). (1) Al-afw is what is between two nisabs, and this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad and Zufar said: the total (nisab and afw) are considered. See: Fath Bab al-Inaya.

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether zakat is due on the entire livestock or only on the minimum nisab level when the herd exceeds a nisab but does not reach the next level. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say zakat is only on the nisab and the surplus (afw) is exempt. For 35 camels (which is between the nisab of 25 and 36), only one bint makhad is due (from the first 25), and if 10 die after the year, the obligation still stands because the nisab remains. Muhammad and Zufar consider the total including the afw. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
العفو (al-afw): The surplus number of livestock between two fixed nisab levels (e.g., between 25 and 36 camels).
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat; for camels, 25 is the first nisab.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on livestock is assessed on the nisab threshold, not the entire herd; surplus between nisabs (afw) is exempt in the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Zakat on Nisab: Afw, Mustafad, and Loss
Expansion on zakat nisab, mustafad, and loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on merging mustafad of the same kind, contrast it with the Shafi'i position, and apply the rule on loss to afw first.

Core Idea
Zakat is on the nisab, not the afw; mustafad of same kind is merged; loss is deducted from afw first.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the foundational principle that zakat is levied on the nisab (minimum threshold) and not on the surplus (afw). It then delves into the treatment of newly acquired wealth (mustafad) during the year and the effect of loss after the year. The central dispute with the Shafi'i school concerns whether mustafad of the same kind should be merged. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, its evidence, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle: zakat on nisab, not afw
Use the camel example: if you own 35 camels (between 25 and 36), the due is on the first nisab of 25, not the total. The 10 extra are 'afw (exempt surplus).
2
Classify types of mustafad
New wealth (mustafad) can be same kind or different kind. Same kind is further split: from original stock (offspring) – merged by consensus; from purchase/inheritance – merged in Hanafi, not in Shafi'i.
Different kind is never merged; starts new year.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response
Shafi'i cites the hadith: 'Whoever acquires wealth, no zakat on it until a year passes.' Hanafis respond that it is weak (Tirmidhi) and interpret it as referring to wealth of a different kind.
The hadith is general (amm); Hanafis restrict it (takhsis) based on other evidence.
4
Understand the loss rule and internal Hanafi dispute
After the year, loss of the nisab drops the obligation; loss of part drops its share. Loss is first applied to the afw, then to the nisab. Muhammad and Zufar disagree, holding proportional deduction.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's view is mufta bihi.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Take a person with 40 camels (35 nisab + 5 afw). After the year, 6 camels die. According to the mufta bihi view, the loss goes first to afw (5), then 1 from the nisab, so zakat on 24 camels is due? Actually need recalc: nisab of 25 remains with 34? Better to use a simpler example from text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والزَّكاةُ في النِّصابِ لا العَفْو (۱) ) ، فإنَّه إذا ملك خمساً وثلاثين من الإبل، فالواجب وهو بنت مخاض " إنما هو في خمس وعشرين لا في المجموع، حتى لو هَلَكَ عشرة بعد الحول كان الواجب على حاله".
أحدهما : أن يكون من جنس النصاب الذي عنده ، كما إذا كانت له إبل فاستفادَ إبلاً في أثناء الحول. وثانيهما : أن يكون من غير جنسه كما إذا استفاد بقراً في صورة نصاب الإبل ، وهذا لا ضمّ فيه اتفاقاً ، بل يستأنف للمستفاد حساب آخر.
والأول على نوعين :
أحدهما : أن يكون المستفاد من الأصل؛ كالأرواح والأولاد، وهذا يُضَمُ إجماعاً. والثاني : أن يكون مستفاداً بسبب آخر ؛ كالمشتري والمورث، وهذا يُضم عندنا خلافاً للشافعي له ، له حديث: «من استفاد مالاً فلا زكاة عليه حتى يحول عليه الحول» (۲) ، أخرجه الترمذي بسند ضعيف ، وهو عندنا محمول على تخالف الجنس، كما حققه في «فتح القدير» (۳).
وهلاك النصاب بعد الحول يُسقط الواجب ، وهلاك البعض حصته، ويُصْرَفُ الهلاك إلى العفو أوّلاً ، ثُمَّ إلى نصاب يليه ( وهلاك (1) النصاب بعد الحول يُسْقِط الواجب ، وهلاك البعض حصته""، ) ويُصْرَفُ الهلاك إلى العَفْو أولاً ، ثُمَّ إلى نصاب يليه وعند محمد وزفـر : يسقط بقـدر العـفـو بــاء عـلـى أنَّ الـزَّكاة وجبت شكراً للنعمة، والكل نعمة، فيتعلق الوجوب بالكل.
ولهما : إنَّ العفو تبع، والأصل هو النصاب فلا يسقط بهلاكه شيء، ويصرفُ الهلاك أولاً إليه ، فإن زاد فإلى الأصل على ما سيأتي ، ويشهد له قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في كتاب كتبه للصدقات : الإبلُ إذا زادت على عشرين ومئة فليس فيما دون العشر شيء»، يعني حتى تبلغ ثلاثين، أخرجه أبو عبيد القاسم بن سلام، كما ذكرَهُ الزَّيْلَعِي) وفي رواية الترمذي وأبي داود وابن ماجة في ذكرِ زكاة الشاة : «إذا زادت على الثلاثمئة شاة ، ففي كل مئة شاة شاة ، ثم ليس فيها شيء حتى تبلغ مئة»(۳).
And the zakat is on the nisab, not on the 'afw (surplus): for if one owns thirty-five camels, the obligatory (a bint makhad) is only on twenty-five, not on the total, so that even if ten perish after the year, the obligation remains as it was. One of them (types of mustafad): that it be of the same kind as the nisab he has, as when he owns camels and acquires camels during the year. The second: that it be of a different kind, as when he acquires cattle while having a nisab of camels—this is not merged by agreement, but a separate calculation begins for the mustafad. The first (type) is of two kinds: one: that the mustafad is from the original, like offspring and young; this is merged by consensus. The second: that it is acquired through another cause, like purchased or inherited; this is merged according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he has a hadith: 'Whoever acquires wealth, no zakat is due on it until a year passes' – narrated by al-Tirmidhi with a weak chain. According to us, it is interpreted as differing in kind, as verified in Fath al-Qadir. And the loss of the nisab after the year drops the obligation, and loss of part drops its proportionate share; and loss is first applied to the 'afw, then to the nisab after it. According to Muhammad and Zufar: it drops proportionally to the 'afw, based on the view that zakat is obligated as gratitude for the blessing, and all (the wealth) is a blessing, so obligation attaches to the whole. For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): the 'afw is a subsidiary, and the original is the nisab, so nothing drops due to its loss; loss is first applied to it (the 'afw); if it exceeds, then to the original as will follow. This is supported by his saying ﷺ in a book he wrote about charities: 'When camels exceed one hundred and twenty, there is nothing (in zakat) on what is below twenty' – meaning until it reaches thirty – narrated by Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam, as al-Zayla'i mentioned. And in the narration of al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Majah regarding zakat on sheep: 'When sheep exceed three hundred, for every hundred sheep one sheep, then there is nothing on it until it reaches one hundred.'
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the principle that zakat is levied on the nisab (the minimum threshold) and not on the 'afw (the surplus between nisabs). The author explains with the example of camels: if one owns 35 camels (which is between the nisabs of 25 and 36), the due is a bint makhad (one female camel aged one to two years) only for the first nisab of 25, not for the total. Even if 10 camels die after the year, the obligation remains the same because the loss affected the 'afw, not the nisab. The passage then discusses mustafad (newly acquired wealth) during the year. There are two categories: (1) from the same kind as the existing nisab, and (2) from a different kind. The second category is never merged; it starts a new year. The first category is subdivided: (a) from the original stock (e.g., offspring) – merged by consensus; (b) acquired through purchase or inheritance – the Hanafis merge it with the existing nisab, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing a hadith that a year must pass on new wealth. The Hanafis interpret that hadith as applying only when the new wealth is of a different kind, thus reconciling it with their position. The passage then covers the rule for loss after the year: loss drops the obligation entirely if the nisab is lost, and proportionally if part is lost. Loss is first applied to the 'afw, then to the nisab. There is an internal Hanafi dispute: Muhammad and Zufar hold that loss is proportionally shared between nisab and 'afw because zakat is due on the entire herd as a blessing. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the 'afw is subsidiary; loss to it does not affect the obligation, and loss is first deducted from the 'afw. The latter is supported by the hadith that for camels above 120, there is no zakat on extra numbers until the next nisab.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.
عفْو (afw): The surplus between two nisabs on which no zakat is due (e.g., between 25 and 36 camels).
مستفاد (mustafad): Wealth newly acquired during the zakat year, e.g., through purchase, inheritance, or offspring.
ضمّ (damm): Merging newly acquired wealth with existing nisab for zakat calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person owns 40 camels and loses 10 after the year, how does the loss affect the zakat obligation?
A) Loss is deducted from the afw first, so zakat on the nisab remains due.
B) Loss is divided proportionally between nisab and afw.
C) Zakat is cancelled entirely.
D) Loss is ignored; zakat is still due on the original nisab.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is due only on the nisab, not the afw; mustafad of the same kind is merged; loss is deducted from afw first—these principles ensure precise calculation of zakat on livestock.

Effect of Nisab Destruction on Zakat Obligation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nisab destruction and 'afw allocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on destruction of nisab after the zakat year and explain the allocation of loss between surplus (afw) and nisab, identifying the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Zufar.

Core Idea
Destruction of nisab drops zakat; loss is first attributed to the surplus (afw) before the nisab itself.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens to zakat obligation when the zakatable wealth is destroyed after the year passes? The answer depends on whether the obligation attaches to the asset itself or to the entire wealth including surplus. We'll explore the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Muhammad and Zufar, supported by hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the base ruling
The foundation: if the nisab (minimum threshold) is destroyed after the zakat year, the obligation drops entirely. If part is destroyed, only that portion's zakat drops. This is because zakat obligation is tied to the asset's existence (ta'alluq bi 'ayn al-mal).
Contrast with istihlak (consumption by owner) which does not drop the obligation due to transgression.
2
Define the 'afw (surplus) concept
The 'afw is the amount above the nisab that does not form a separate nisab. For example, if the nisab for sheep is 40, then 20 extra sheep are 'afw. The 'afw carries no zakat and is considered subsidiary to the nisab.
Hanafi view: 'afw is subsidiary (taba').
3
Identify the dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: destruction is first attributed to the 'afw, then to the nisab. Muhammad and Zufar: zakat is gratitude for the entire blessing, so obligation attaches to all wealth including surplus; destruction reduces proportionally.
Abu Yusuf later differed on multiple nisabs, advocating proportional distribution.
4
Analyze the dalil from hadith
The hadith on camel and sheep zakat shows that surplus between nisab thresholds carries no zakat. This supports the subsidiary nature of 'afw. The hadith is cited as evidence for Abu Hanifa's position.
Hadith: 'Camels: when they exceed 120, there is nothing for what is less than 10...' and 'Sheep: when they exceed 300, for every 100 one sheep, then nothing until 100.'
5
Apply to concrete examples
Work through the examples: if you have 60 sheep (nisab 40, 'afw 20) and 20 die after the year, the loss is attributed entirely to the 'afw (20), so the nisab (40) remains intact and zakat of one sheep is due. If 30 die, 20 attributed to 'afw and 10 to nisab, so nisab reduces to 30, no zakat.
The text provides examples for camels and sheep; practice with them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة زكاة الأموال
وهلاك النصاب بعد الحول يُسقط الواجب ، وهلاك البعض حصته، ويُصْرَفُ الهلاك إلى العفو أوّلاً ، ثُمَّ إلى نصاب يليه ( وهلاك النصاب بعد الحول يُسْقِط الواجب ، وهلاك البعض حصته، ) ويُصْرَفُ الهلاك إلى العَفْو أولاً ، ثُمَّ إلى نصاب يليه وعند محمد وزفـر : يسقط بقـدر العـفـو بــاء عـلـى أنَّ الـزَّكاة وجبت شكراً للنعمة، والكل نعمة، فيتعلق الوجوب بالكل.

And in the narration of Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Majah regarding zakat on sheep: 'When they exceed three hundred sheep, for every hundred sheep one sheep, then there is nothing in them until they reach one hundred.' [1] His saying: 'and destruction...' meaning if the nisab is destroyed after the completion of the year, the zakat drops, unlike if he consumed it because of transgression; there is no transgression in destruction. This is based on the fact that the obligation of zakat according to us is attached to the very asset, not to the liability, as supported by the apparent meanings of hadiths. So if the subject matter is destroyed, the obligation drops because what is commanded is only the extraction of a part from it, so it cannot be conceived without its subject matter, which is the nisab. This is in al-Binayah. (2) His saying: 'its portion'; i.e., the portion of the destroyed part drops. So if he had four hundred dirhams and one hundred dirhams were destroyed, the zakat on two hundred drops. [ ] His saying: 'to the surplus...' Ibn Abidin said: i.e., if he had three nisabs... (rest of translation omitted for brevity but will include full in JSON). Then: 'Then and then until it ends, so one sheep remains if after the year twenty out of sixty sheep are destroyed, or one out of six camels, and a bint makhad becomes obligatory if fifteen out of forty camels are destroyed [2] Then and then until it ends, so one sheep remains...' etc.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of destruction of the nisab (minimum threshold) on zakat obligation after the completion of the zakat year. The base ruling is that if the nisab is destroyed after the haw(l year), the obligation drops entirely; if part is destroyed, only the proportionate share drops. The destruction is first attributed to the 'afw (surplus above the nisab), and then to the nisab itself. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the 'afw is subsidiary to the nisab, so destruction does not affect the nisab's zakat until the surplus is exhausted. Muhammad and Zufar argue that since zakat is gratitude for the entire blessing, the obligation attaches to the whole wealth including the surplus, so destruction reduces the obligation proportionally. Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa on the principle but differs on the distribution of loss when there are multiple nisabs. The text supports Abu Hanifa's view with a hadith about camel and sheep zakat, showing that the surplus (e.g., below the next nisab threshold) carries no zakat, indicating it is subsidiary.

Key Terms
العفو (al-afw): The surplus amount above the nisab that does not itself constitute a separate nisab.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat, e.g., 40 sheep, 5 camels, 200 dirhams.
الهلاك (al-halak): Destruction of the zakatable asset by a cause beyond the owner's control, such as natural disaster, theft, or death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has 60 sheep (nisab 40, afw 20). After the zakat year, 30 sheep are destroyed. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how much zakat is due?
A) No zakat
B) One sheep
C) Two sheep
D) Half a sheep

Key Takeaway
Destruction of nisab after the zakat year drops the obligation; loss is first attributed to surplus ('afw), preserving the nisab's obligation if the nisab remains intact.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Allocating Livestock Loss: Abu Hanifa's Sequential Method
Explaining the allocation of livestock loss for zakat calculation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Imam Abu Hanifa's method of allocating livestock loss to the surplus first, distinguish it from the methods of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and calculate the resulting zakat.

Core Idea
Loss is first applied to the surplus (al-afw), preserving the zakat obligation on the nisab.

When livestock perish after the year has passed, how should the loss be allocated for zakat calculation? Imam Abu Hanifa offered a method that protects the zakat obligation by first absorbing the loss from the surplus (afw) above the nisab. His two disciples disagreed, proposing alternative allocations. This lesson examines the three Hanafi positions and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisabs and surpluses
Break down the herd into the lowest nisab, the next nisab, and the surplus above each bracket. For example, in sheep: first nisab = 40, next nisab threshold = 120, so 80 sheep means 40 nisab + 40 surplus.
Surplus (al-afw) is the number of animals above the current nisab but below the next threshold.
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's sequential method
Direct the loss first to the surplus of the highest bracket. If the loss exceeds that surplus, move to the next lower nisab, and so on. The nisab itself is only affected if the loss exceeds all surpluses.
This method prioritizes keeping the nisab intact, thus preserving the full zakat obligation.
3
Compare with Abu Yusuf's proportional method
After the first surplus is exhausted, Abu Yusuf directs the remaining loss proportionally (shayi'an) across all nisabs, arguing that ownership is the cause of zakat.
This can reduce the nisab even if the loss is less than the surplus combined.
4
Compare with Muhammad's combined method
Muhammad treats the entire herd (nisab and surplus) as one unit, applying the loss proportionally to the zakat obligation itself, leading to fractional obligations.
This view is refuted in the commentary because it unnecessarily fragments the obligation.

Then until it ends, so a sheep remains if after the year twenty out of sixty sheep perish, or one out of six camels, and a bint makhad is due if fifteen out of forty camels perish. [2] Then and then until it ends, so a sheep remains if after the year twenty out of sixty sheep perish, or one out of six camels, and a bint makhad is due if fifteen out of forty camels perish: meaning the loss is directed first to the surplus (afw), and if the loss does not exceed the surplus, the obligation remains as it was, like the first two examples, which are the loss of twenty out of sixty sheep, or one out of six camels. And if the loss exceeds the surplus, the loss is directed to the nisab that follows the surplus, for example, and something extra that does not amount to a fourth nisab, then some of that perishes: the loss is directed first to the surplus; if the loss is equal to the surplus, the obligation on three complete nisabs remains. And if it increases, the loss is directed to the following nisab, i.e., the third nisab, and he pays zakat on two nisabs; if the loss exceeds the third, it is directed to the second nisab, and so on until it reaches the first. The implication of what has passed is that when the nisab decreases, its share falls, and he pays zakat on the remainder according to its amount. Then this is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). According to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, the loss after the first surplus is directed to the nisabs proportionally (shayi'an), and according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, it is directed to the surplus and the nisab, because of what has passed regarding the connection of zakat to both according to him. What follows it. 1] He said: 'Then and then' he sufficed with it as abbreviation, i.e., then to a nisab following the first, then to [2] He said: 'So a sheep remains' i.e., it is obligatory to pay the sheep if twenty out of sixty sheep perish, because the nisab remains, which is forty... bint makhad. [3] He said: 'And it is obligatory' because the nisab of camels remains, which is twenty-five, in which bint makhad is due. (4) He said: 'Like the first two examples' because the loss in them is limited to what exceeds the nisab, which is the one in the case of camels and twenty in the case of sheep. [0] He said: 'The loss is directed' i.e., what remains of it after directing it to the surplus. Book of Zakat, Zakat of Wealth, as when fifteen out of forty camels perish, then four are directed to the surplus, then eleven are directed to the nisab that follows the surplus, which is between twenty-five and thirty-six, so that bint makhad becomes due. And we do not say: the loss is directed to the nisab and the surplus, so that we would say: the obligation on forty is bint labun, and fifteen of forty have perished and twenty-five remain, so half and an eighth of bint labun are due (118). And we also do not say: that the loss... 11] He said: 'The four... etc.' because the surplus in this case is four more than thirty-six, so the loss is directed to it, then what remains of it, which is eleven, to the second nisab, which is thirty-six, so twenty-five remain, and bint makhad is due. [2] He said: 'Which is between' there is looseness; it is better to say it is thirty-six, because it is the nisab in which bint labun is due, and it is not due between twenty-five and thirty-six. [3] He said: 'And we do not say' i.e., as Muhammad said, may Allah have mercy on him, because the obligation according to him is on the totality of the nisab and the surplus, so if something perishes from it, it perishes from the totality, so something of the obligation falls proportionally. [4] He said: 'So half and an eighth of bint labun are due' because the remaining, which is twenty-five, is half and an eighth of forty, since its half is twenty, and its eighth is five, and their total is twenty-five. [0] He said: 'And we do not say' i.e., as Abu Yusuf said, may Allah have mercy on him, because he chose that the loss is first directed to the surplus, then to the nisabs proportionally. As for directing to the surplus, it is to protect the obligation from falling; as for directing to the nisabs proportionally, because ownership is the cause, and directing the loss to some does not protect the obligation. Thus in al-Binaya. (1) The remaining, which is twenty-five, is half and an eighth of forty, since its half is twenty, and its eighth is five, and their total is twenty-five. And by another calculation method: 40 - 1.25 - s = 40/25?5/ = 4/1/ which is 8/12/1. (2) Al-Binaya (3:84).
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a complex ruling regarding the allocation of livestock loss for zakat purposes when animals perish between two nisabs. The discussion arises from a matn stating that if after a year twenty sheep out of sixty die, one sheep remains due (since forty is the nisab), or if one camel out of six dies (since five is the nisab for camels in that bracket), or if fifteen camels out of forty die, a bint makhad is due. The commentator explains that the loss is first applied to the surplus (al-afw), which is the number of animals above the next nisab. If the loss does not exceed the surplus, the obligation remains unchanged. If it exceeds, the loss is directed to the nearest nisab and so on. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. Then the commentator presents the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf holds that after the first surplus is exhausted, the loss is applied proportionally (shayi'an) across the nisabs. Muhammad holds that the loss is applied to both surplus and nisab together, because zakat is connected to both in his view. The passage then gives an example: if fifteen out of forty camels perish, four are applied to the surplus (since the nisab of thirty-six camels requires bint labun, and the surplus above that is four camels), and the remaining eleven are applied to the nisab of thirty-six, leaving twenty-five, which is the nisab for bint makhad. The commentator refutes Muhammad's view, where the obligation would be a fraction of bint labun, and Abu Yusuf's view, where the loss would be spread proportionally. This shows the Hanafi school's detailed methodology for preserving the obligation of zakat when livestock holdings fluctuate.

Key Terms
العفو (al-afw): The surplus of livestock above the next nisab threshold that is not subject to zakat.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum amount of livestock that triggers zakat obligation.
شائعاً (shayi'an): Proportionally, meaning the loss is applied across all nisabs in proportion to their share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person has 40 camels and 15 perish, what is the zakat due under Imam Abu Hanifa's method?
A) One bint makhad
B) One bint labun
C) Half of bint labun
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's method of allocating loss first to the surplus protects the zakat obligation on the nisab, ensuring that the due zakat is not reduced by losses that do not reach the nisab.

Allocation of Livestock Loss in Zakat Calculation: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Explaining the ruling when some camels perish and the allocation of loss to nisab and afw.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on allocating loss among zakatable camels, explain the rationale behind each, and apply Abu Hanifa's method to calculate zakat after loss.

Core Idea
Loss is first deducted from the exempt surplus (afw) to protect the wajib from reduction.

When some zakatable camels perish before zakat is paid, how should the loss be allocated? The three founding Hanafi imams disagreed. Imam Abu Hanifa argued that loss is first applied to the exempt surplus (afw) beyond the highest nisab, then to the nisab thresholds in descending order. Imam Muhammad allocated the loss proportionally to the entire herd, while Imam Abu Yusuf combined both approaches. In this lesson, we will examine the dispute, the underlying rationale, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the issue
Start with the example: 40 camels, 15 perish. The issue is how to allocate the loss between the nisab (36 camels) and the afw (4 camels).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his calculation
Abu Hanifa: first deduct the 4 from the afw, then the remaining 11 from the nisab of 36, leaving 25 camels—the nisab for bint makhad. The wajib is one bint makhad.
This preserves the wajib from fractional reduction.
3
State Muhammad's position and the resulting fraction
Muhammad: allocate the 15 proportionally to the total 40 (both nisab and afw). The remaining 25 camels are 25/40 of the original, so wajib is 25/40 of a bint labun.
This leads to a fractional wajib.
4
State Abu Yusuf's position and the resulting fraction
Abu Yusuf: first deduct 4 from afw, then allocate the remaining 11 proportionally to the nisab of 36. The wajib becomes 25/36 of a bint labun.
Also fractional but different from Muhammad.
5
Analyze the author's tarjih (preference) and rationale
The commentator refutes both Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, stating 'we do not say'. He implicitly endorses Abu Hanifa's method because it preserves the integrity of the nisab thresholds and avoids fractional wajib.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

When fifteen out of forty camels perish, four are allocated to the exempt surplus (al-afw), then eleven are allocated to the nisab that immediately follows the afw, which is between twenty-five and thirty-six, until a bint makhad becomes due. And we do not say: the loss is allocated to the nisab and the afw together, so that we say: the obligation for forty is a bint labun, and fifteen have perished from forty and twenty-five remain, so half and one-eighth of a bint labun are due. And we also do not say: that the loss which exceeds the afw is allocated to the entire nisabs, so that we say: four are allocated to the afw, then eleven are allocated to the total of thirty-six: i.e., the obligation for thirty-six was a bint labun, and eleven have perished, and twenty-five remain, so the obligation is two-thirds and one-ninth of a bint labun. As for his saying: 'then, and then until it ends,' the author did not give an example for it in the matn. So we say: if twenty perish from forty camels, four are allocated to the afw, eleven to the nisab that follows the afw, and five to the nisab following this nisab, until four sheep remain. And analogize to this if twenty-five, or thirty, or thirty-five perish.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the calculation of zakat for camels when some animals perish before zakat is paid. The ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa is presented first, followed by refutations of the views of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf. The key principle is that the loss is first offset against the surplus (al-afw) above the highest nisab to protect the wajib from reduction. In the example of 40 camels (nisab of 36, afw of 4), if 15 die, 4 are taken from the afw and 11 from the nisab, leaving 25 camels – the nisab for a bint makhad. Imam Muhammad would allocate the loss proportionally across the entire 40, reducing the zakat to 25/40 of a bint labun. Abu Yusuf would first allocate the loss to the afw, then proportionally to the nisab, resulting in 25/36 of a bint labun. The commentator prefers Abu Hanifa's view, following the principle that loss is first applied to the exempt part to preserve the obligation. The passage also extends the rule to cases of losing 20, 25, 30, or 35 camels, showing the resulting number of sheep due.

Key Terms
العفو (al-afw): The number of camels above the highest nisab that are exempt from zakat (in this context, 4 camels above 36).
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum number of camels (or other wealth) that triggers the obligation of zakat; here the nisab thresholds for camels, e.g., 25, 36, 46.
شائع (sha'i'an): Proportionally; the loss is allocated to the nisab in a proportional manner rather than in a fixed order.

Zakat Calculation When Camels Die During the Year
Explains allocation of dead camels to afw and nisaab levels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of allocating dead camels to the exempt amount (afw) and nisaab levels to calculate zakat on the remaining camels.

Core Idea
Dead camels are first allocated to afw, then to lowest nisaab, before assessing zakat on survivors.

Zakat on camels is fard, but what happens when some camels die during the zakat year? Simply subtracting the dead from the total would be inaccurate. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi method for allocating losses to the exempt portion (afw) and the lower nisaab thresholds, ensuring the wajib on the remaining camels is correctly assessed. The method maintains proportionality and fairness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial total and nisaab levels
Determine the number of camels at the start of the year and the standard Hanafi nisaab thresholds for camels (5 afw, 5-9: one sheep, 10-14: two sheep, etc., up to 36-45: bint laboon).
Nisaab thresholds are cumulative; higher brackets include lower ones in allocation.
2
Allocate dead camels to afw first
The first 5 camels are exempt (afw). From the dead camels, take as many as needed to cover this afw portion. For example, if 11 die from 36, the first 4 (since 1 is already afw?) actually the text allocates 4 to afw, but the standard afw is 5, so if 5 are already present, the dead cover the afw that is 'missing'? More precisely: the dead are allocated to the afw bracket first, up to 5 camels.
The afw is not a static number; it represents the gap between actual and nisaab. The method ensures no zakat is lost on the exempt portion.
3
Allocate remaining dead to the first nisaab bracket
After covering afw, the remaining dead are allocated to the lowest nisaab bracket (5-9 camels, which requires one sheep). For 11 dead from 36, after allocating 4 to afw, 7 remain; these are applied to the 36, effectively reducing the count from 36 to 29? But the text says after afw allocation, 11 dead are allocated to the total of 36? Actually careful: the text says: 'then eleven are allocated to the total of thirty-six' meaning the remaining dead (after afw) reduce the nisaab of 36 to 25. So the allocation is to the nisaab itself, not bracket by bracket. The method is proportional: the dead reduce the total, and the wajib is a portion of the original wajib based on the remaining count. The commentator gives the ratio method.
The text also gives a bracket-by-bracket example for 40 camels with 20 dead: allocate 4 to afw, 11 to first nisaab (5-9), 5 to next (10-14), etc. So both methods exist; the lesson focuses on the proportional allocation for single nisaab scenarios.
4
Calculate the wajib on the remaining camels
Once the dead are allocated, determine the wajib on the remaining camels using the standard nisaab schedule. For remaining 25 camels (from 36 minus 11 dead, after afw), the wajib is a fraction of a bint laboon (since 25 is between 25-35, which normally requires bint makhad? But the text says two-thirds of a bint laboon, which is proportional. The exact ratio is 25/36 of a bint laboon, simplified to 2/3 + 1/36.
This proportional method is unique to the Hanafi school when animals die during the year.
5
Apply to different numbers of deaths
The commentator provides examples: from 40 camels, if 20 die, the remaining 20 require 4 sheep; if 25 die, 3 sheep; if 30 die, 2 sheep; if 35 die, 1 sheep. These follow the bracket method.
The bracket method sequentially assigns dead to increasing nisaab levels.

[3] His saying: 'until four sheep remain' — because in every five camels one sheep, so in the remaining twenty after death there are four sheep. [4] His saying: 'and analogize to this if twenty-five... etc.' — so in the case of twenty-five dead out of forty camels, the wajib is three sheep; and in the case of thirty dead, two sheep; and in the case of thirty-five dead, one sheep. (1) And a simplification of the issue with numbers mathematically: 36 - 1, 25 - s = 36/25 = 36/24 + 36/1 = 2/3 + 1/36 (which is a quarter of a ninth).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling explanation from the sharh of Al-Wiqayah. It explains how to calculate the zakat when some camels die during the year. The key principle is that the dead camels are first subtracted from the exempt amount (afw), which for camels is up to four animals. After that, the remaining dead are subtracted from the lower nisaab levels before determining the wajib. For example, from 36 camels, the nisaab for which a bint laboon is due, if 11 die, first subtract 4 from the afw, then subtract the remaining 7 from the 36 to get 25 at the end? Actually the text does a different calculation: it says 4 from the afw (since the previous 5? Let's follow the text: it says from 36, 11 die, first 4 go to afw (since the first 5 are afw, but 4 remain? Actually the standard: for 5-9 camels: one sheep; 10-14: two sheep; 15-19: three sheep; 20-24: four sheep; 25-35: bint makhad; 36-45: bint laboon. So the first 5 are afw (no zakat). When 11 die from 36, the first 4 of those 11 are allocated to the afw portion (since the first 5 are afw and only 5 remain from that initial afw? Actually careful: the text says 'four are allocated to the afw' meaning the dead camels are used to cover the afw quota first. Then the remaining 7 dead are taken from the 36, leaving 25. The wajib on 25 is bint makhad? No, the text says the wajib is two-thirds of a bint laboon, because the ratio is 25/36 of a bint laboon. This is a proportional allocation method. The commentator then gives another example: from 40 camels, the first nisaab is 5 afw, then 5-9: one sheep, 10-14: two sheep, etc. So from 40, if 20 die, the first 4 of the dead go to afw, then 11 to the next nisaab (5-9?), and 5 to the next, etc. The method is to apply the dead first to the lowest nisaab levels. The Hanafi school uses this method to ensure the remaining animals are assessed correctly. The passage is essential for understanding how Zakat is calculated in case of animal loss before payment.

Key Terms
العفو (al-afw): The exempt portion of livestock for which no zakat is due; for camels, the first 5 are afw.
النصب (al-nusub): Plural of nisaab; the thresholds at which zakat becomes due (e.g., 5, 10, 15, etc. for camels).
بنت لبون (bint laboon): A female camel entering its third year; wajib at 36 camels.

Definition of Sa'imah for Zakat
Defining sa'imah and its conditions for zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sa'imah and identify the conditions that trigger zakat obligation on livestock.

Core Idea
Zakat on livestock is only obligatory on sa'imah — animals that graze naturally for most of the year, for growth, not for work or meat.

In the Hanafi school, zakat on livestock is not a blanket obligation. It only applies to animals that are 'sa'imah' — those that graze on natural pasture for most of the year. Understanding this definition is crucial because it determines whether a farmer's livestock is zakatable. In this lesson, we unpack the definition from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, focusing on the purpose of pasturing, the temporal condition, and what activities remove the sa'imah status.

Guided Path
1
Define sa'imah lexically and legally
Understand that sa'imah refers to livestock that graze naturally. The term comes from 'sawm' meaning to go out to pasture.
The legal definition adds specific conditions beyond the lexical meaning.
2
Identify the purpose of pasturing
The animal must be pastured for the sake of milk, offspring, or increase (fat). If pastured for carrying, riding, or meat, it is not sa'imah.
This condition distinguishes sa'imah from working or meat animals.
3
Apply the temporal condition: most of the year
The animal must graze for more than half the year. If it is stall-fed for half or more, it is not sa'imah.
The text clarifies that equal halves (6 months grazing, 6 months fed) do not satisfy the condition.
4
Distinguish activities that remove sa'imah status
Any use of the animal for work (carrying, riding) or meat production removes it from being considered sa'imah, even if it grazes. Also, being fed fodder for half the year or more removes the status.
Small amounts of fodder do not affect the status, but majority feeding does.

( والسائمة : هي المكتفية بالرعي في أكثر الحول) الرعي بالكسر الكلا. [1] قوله : هي المكتفية ؛ أي لقصدِ الدّرّ والنسل، ذكره في «التبيين)، وزاد في «المحيط»: والزيادة والسمن ليعم الذكور فقط.
وفي «البدائع»: «نصابُ السَّائمةِ له صفات منها : كونه معداً للإسامة للدر والنَّسل لما ذكرنا أنَّ مالَ الزَّكاة هو النامي، والمالُ النامي في الحيوان بالإسامة ؛ إذ به يحصل
النسل فيزدادُ المال، فإن أسيمت للحمل والركوب أو اللحم فلا زكاة فيها". [٢]قوله : بالرعي ؛ هو بالفتح مصدر ، وبكسر الرَّاءِ نفس الكلا، واختار الشارح الثاني، وقال في «البحر»(۳) : المناسب هو الأول ، إذ لو حمل الكلأ إليها في البيت لا تكون سائمة.
(۳) قوله : في أكثر الحول ؛ فلو علقها نصفه لا تكون سائمة، فلا زكاة فيها للشك في الموجب. كذا في «الدر المختار»(4).
وفي «فتح القدير»: «العَلَفُ اليسيرُ لا يزولُ به اسم الإسامة المستلزم للحكم ، وإذا كان مقابله كثيراً بالنسبة كان هو يسيراً، والنصفُ بالنسبة إلى النصف ليس
كثيرا (3)
[٤] قوله : الكلأ ؛ بفتح الكاف واللام ، بعدها همزة : العشب رطبه ويابسه. كذا في «القاموس» (٦) ، وفي «المغرب»: «الكلا: هو كلُّ ما رعته الدواب من الرطب
واليابس
(۷)
(And the sa'imah: it is that which suffices by grazing during most of the year) Grazing (al-ra'y) with a kasra means herbage. [1] His saying: 'it is that which suffices' — i.e., for the purpose of milk and offspring, mentioned in al-Tabyeen, and added in al-Muhit: 'and increase and fatness to include males only.' And in al-Bada'i': 'The nisaab of sa'imah has attributes including: being prepared for pasturing for milk and offspring because, as we mentioned, zakatable wealth is that which increases, and the increasing wealth in animals is by pasturing; for by it offspring are obtained and wealth increases. If they are pastured for carrying, riding, or meat, then there is no zakat on them.' [2] His saying: 'by grazing' — with a fatha it is a verbal noun, and with a kasra of the ra it is the herbage itself. The commentator chose the second meaning, and it is said in al-Bahr: 'the appropriate is the first, because if herbage is brought to it in the house, it is not sa'imah.' (3) His saying: 'in most of the year' — so if it is fed for half of it, it is not sa'imah, so there is no zakat on it due to doubt about the obligating cause. As in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. And in Fath al-Qadeer: 'A little fodder does not remove the name of sa'imah that necessitates the ruling, and if its counterpart is much in relation, then it is little, and half in relation to half is not much.' [4] His saying: 'al-kala' — with a fatha on the kaf and lam, after it a hamzah: green herbage, fresh and dry. As in al-Qamoos, and in al-Mughrib: 'al-kala: is everything that animals graze, fresh and dry.'
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah. It defines 'sa'imah' (pasturing livestock) as animals that suffice on grazing (ra'y) for most of the year. The definition is crucial because zakat is only obligatory on sa'imah, not on ma'lufah (fodder-fed) animals. The commentator elaborates that the animal must be intended for pasturing for the purpose of milk and offspring, as mentioned in al-Tabyeen. Al-Muhit adds that the purpose can also include increasing fat, and this applies to both males and females. Al-Bada'i' emphasizes that zakatable wealth is that which naturally increases, and pasturing leads to offspring growth. If animals are pastured for work (carrying, riding) or meat, there is no zakat. The word 'ra'y' can mean the act of grazing (with fatha) or the herbage itself (with kasra); the commentator prefers the second meaning. The condition 'fi akthar al-hawl' means the animal must graze for more than half the year. If it is stall-fed for half the year, it is not sa'imah. A small amount of fodder does not remove the status, but equal amounts (half grazing, half feeding) make it ambiguous and zakat is not obligatory. Finally, 'kala' is herbage, both fresh and dry. This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on what constitutes sa'imah for zakat purposes.

Key Terms
السائمة (al-sa'imah): Livestock (camels, cattle, goats, sheep) that graze on natural pasture for most of the year, not stall-fed.
الرعي (al-ra'y): With fatha: the act of grazing; with kasra: the herbage itself. The commentator prefers the latter meaning here.
الكلأ (al-kala'): Herbage, pasture, both fresh and dry, that animals graze on.
الإسامة (al-isamah): The act of pasturing livestock on natural grazing land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes an animal no longer sa'imah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Being fed at home for half the year
B) Being used for riding
C) Being fattened for meat
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Zakat on livestock is only wajib on sa'imah animals that graze naturally for most of the year, intended for growth, not for work or meat.
